小說

五家鎭上一件大事（六） 224

— 張一蘋

富公公的塡房舅兄朱全貴，他起初是站在伍老太爺身旁的。他接受了妹子的哭訴，今天預備來說幾句撑頭話的，因爲屬於她面上的只有如哥哥一個人。女人家雖蠻不講理，這類事的勝敗在五家鎭上已有過不少先例，今天這末許多衣冠楚楚的親戚全集，站在富生方面說話的又佔了十分之九，所以她重託了哥哥帮這忙的。然而哥哥不是妹妹，他一見伍老太爺的來勢兇兇，他不能吃這了眼前虧，偷偷地溜出這周圍和他兩個小外甥打混去了。

富公公仰起頭來，都是那樣虎視耽耽的眼睛。他肚子裏再有一筆沒有說出來的債項！富生做親事的費用，已被伍老太爺硬生生地劃入賬內了。於是他硬着頭皮說：

「大伯伯，我素來不做虧心事的，弟媳年靑守寡，富生更是我的親兒子，不過…二年災荒，從前戰時事，到上海避難也化費許多錢，這一次富生討親我還負了債哩。」

伍老太爺似乎生氣了，手掌輕輕地在紫檀几上一擊，富公公忙低下頭去，他不明白自己說錯了什麼話，甚至自己說了些什麼。

「富明，我們伍家不能做出這樣不名譽的事，」老太爺一點沒有情面的說「你是要體面的人，等我查考歷年賬簿的時候，大家沒有面子了！」

「大伯伯，不要生氣…」富公公話沒有說完，一個使女從內堂出來說太太請老爺進去，這更使富公公急不出話了。他兩脚沒有移動地位的踏了幾步，終於像兎脫一般一溜烟的朝裏了。

小組會議立刻紛紛地談論起來，蓋住了送來的蟬聲。伍老太爺拍着富生的肩頭，「有我伍公公在，總不會呌你吃虧」。張得福嘻嘻的笑了，他覺得自己的計劃沒有失敗。

朱金貴同兩個小外甥不知什麼時候溜走了，大廳上差不多是淸一色的富生派，張得福自然是最出力的一員，兩位姑老爺和姑太太也早看不過富公公的怕老婆樣子，他們今天不怕大熱天趕到準備有一番口舌，但見伍老太爺打在頭陣，已完全操了勝利，每個人都得意地掛着微笑。

Page 23

1934.08.27

Bohai Bay 1

Japanese Fleet Begins Exercises

Imamura Inspects from Izumo Battleship

Loud Cannon Fire Outside Dagu Port

Navigation Prohibited Within Six Nautical Miles

Japanese Army and Air Force Continue Exercises at Yuguan

(Tianjin) At 9:35 AM today, Imamura Nobujiro, commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, along with his staff, departed Tianjin by the Beining Railway to Tanggu. At 10:35 AM, they transferred at Tanggu to the Izumo, the flagship of the Japanese Third Fleet stationed there, and sailed to the waters outside Dagu Port to inspect the ships participating in the exercise. At 2:10 PM this afternoon, the Third Fleet, consisting of fourteen warships, gathered outside Dagu Port, formed a long line, and Imamura conducted an inspection ceremony aboard the flagship Izumo. Then, the exercise began. The exercise today lasted from 2:30 PM to 5:30 PM, with the 26th and 27th Destroyer Squadrons as the main force. The 10th Squadron of torpedo boats and cruisers served as the hypothetical enemy, sailing from the Hawaiian route, attempting to peer into the Korean Strait. The 26th and 27th Squadrons were ordered to intercept the enemy ships in the waters outside Dagu Port, forming a semicircular formation to attack and bombard the enemy ships. The commander of the hypothetical enemy fleet was Naval Captain Takasu Shiro, Chief of Staff of the Third Fleet. The commander of the hypothetical Imperial fleet was Naval Captain Suga Hikojiro, commander of the 27th Destroyer Squadron. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The ships of the Japanese Third Expeditionary Fleet stationed at Tanggu, on the 25th and 26th, sailed into Dagu Port to conduct a sea blockade exercise in the area west of Tanggu. Japanese residents of Tianjin began visiting to observe from the 24th, and the number has now reached 500. This morning, Imamura went to Tanggu, and after arriving, transferred to a small boat from the Izumo flagship to exit the port. It is scheduled to begin this afternoon, observing naval maneuvers for a week before going to Qingdao. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) A certain diplomatic figure said that Japan has a total of three fleets nationwide. The commander of the Third Fleet is Lieutenant General Imamura. The fleet includes destroyer squadrons, cruiser squadrons, torpedo boat squadrons, submarine squadrons, aircraft carriers, and various types of large and small ships, totaling thirty-six. The commanders stationed at various ports along our coast and in Taiwan serve two-year terms. Each commander must complete their inspection work during their term. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the cessation of the large-scale Japanese military exercise at Qinhuangdao and Yuguan, the Japanese troops who had been dispatched from Beiping and Tianjin to participate are scheduled to board trains on the 31st at Yuqin to return to their posts. The Beining Railway Bureau has prepared the necessary vehicles. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The large-scale Japanese military exercise at Yuguan began at 2:00 PM on the 25th. Traffic was blocked from outside Xiguan to the Japanese barracks south of the railway and the Sipingtai area near Yuguan. Approximately 800 participating soldiers conducted exercises in batches. On the 25th, street fighting was practiced within Yuguan, and field exercises were practiced at Sipingtai. Five airplanes were dispatched from the Japanese airfield in Jinzhou to participate in the Sipingtai exercises. The exercises ended at 4:30 PM and continued on the 26th. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese Third Fleet will begin exercises in Bohai Bay starting on the 26th. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Vice Consul Tanaka of the Japanese Consulate in Tianjin, Kishida, the chairman of the Concession Administrative Committee, Miura, the police chief, and over a hundred Japanese residents, along with over a hundred veterans and members of the volunteer corps, accompanied Commander Imamura of the fleet aboard the Izumo battleship to the waters off Dagu Port at 9:35 AM this morning to observe the Japanese naval exercises. Today, the Tianjin Customs announced that all ships entering and exiting the port must cease navigation in the area six nautical miles outside the Jianggsha reef outside Dagu Port from 1:30 PM to 6:00 PM to avoid danger. At approximately 2:00 PM this afternoon, loud cannon fire erupted outside Dagu Port, and fishing boats and small craft all sailed into Donggu to dock. (26th Special Dispatch)

Huang Fu and Yin Tong 2

Enter Beijing by Steamer from Xunyang

Acceptance of Eastern Tombs Awaits Resolution After Huang Returns to Beiping

(Nanjing) Xunyang Dispatch: Huang Fu and Yin Tong are taking a steamer to Beijing this afternoon, the 26th, and are expected to arrive on the afternoon of the 27th. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The acceptance of the Eastern Tombs has been delayed due to transportation obstructions and the fact that the Preservation Committee has not yet been organized. It is said that a resolution will be reached after Huang Fu returns to Beiping. The security force is currently stationed temporarily in Shimen Town awaiting orders. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) A source familiar with the matter said that negotiations regarding the acceptance of Malanyu have been completely halted. This issue will be addressed with the Japanese side after Huang returns north. Tao Shangming will not be going to Lushan for the time being. He denies having received a telegram from Chiang Kai-shek summoning him. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Jiujiang) Huang Fu and Yin Tong completed their affairs in Guling and descended the mountain on the morning of the 26th. They boarded a steamer in Xunyang at 10:00 AM to go to Beijing, intending to seek instructions from the central government before proceeding to Beiping to take up their duties. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

President Wang Arrives in Beijing Yesterday 3

(Nanjing) President Wang went to Shanghai a few days ago to have Dr. Noel examine his old ailment. Having completed this, he left Shanghai by train at 11:00 PM on the 25th and arrived in Beijing at 7:00 AM on the 26th. After disembarking, Wang went directly to his official residence in the Ministry of Railways to rest. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Xifengkou and Lengkou Branch Customs Offices 4

May Be Established in Early Next Month

(Beiping) Gao Yuanji wrote to Beiping stating that the Xifengkou and Lengkou branch customs offices may be established in early next month. However, bandits are active in Jielingkou, making it difficult to set up a customs office. Gao is currently staying in Qian'an County. (26th Special Dispatch)

Yin Rugeng Returns to Beiping from Tianjin 5

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng is returning to Beiping at 8:00 PM tonight. He will go to Tongxian on the 27th to hold a Confucius worship ceremony and return to Tianjin that evening. All procedures for the acceptance of Malanyu have been completed, and it is only awaiting the receding of floodwaters and the restoration of transportation before taking over. (26th Special Dispatch)

Confucius' Birthday Commemoration 6

Sacrificial Rites Held This Morning in Qufu

(Jinan) This morning, Li Shuchun and He Siyuan took a special train south from Jinan and arrived in Tai'an at noon. When Ye Chucang boarded the train, Chu Minyi and representatives from various ministries and departments had already arrived before reaching Yanzhou. Chu also brought two cameras to film. They then traveled by car to Qufu, where they rested at the Duke Yansheng's Mansion. Kong Decheng hosted a tour of the Confucius Temple. Sacrificial utensils and musical instruments were being arranged. It was decided that drums would be sounded at 7:00 AM on the 27th to gather for the sacrificial ceremony. In the afternoon at 1:00 PM, they will visit the mausoleum. Ye, Chu, and others will return to the Railway Hotel in Yanzhou tonight and return to Qufu on the morning of the 27th for the sacrificial ceremony before Chu returns to Beijing and the others go to Tai'an, planning to climb the mountain on the 28th. The national government's prayer is as follows: "Oh, venerable teacher, model for all generations, illuminating virtue and renewing the people, knowing transformation and fathoming the divine. Reconciling the Six Arts, like the North Star. The world is for all, great unity is admired. Valuing talent and utilizing ability, not for oneself. Only our founding father, broadly imparted this meaning. Concern for the Xia people, fearing barbarians. Brightening the foolish, strengthening the weak, the standard for the nation. Loving one's relatives and being benevolent to the people, showing the righteous way. Selecting the virtuous and enabling the capable, expanding the people's rights. Having become prosperous, what more is needed? Wealth and education. Worrying about inequality, plans for people's livelihood are effective. Thinking about subtle words, combining virtue and communicating with each other. Hundreds of generations will benefit, steering this grand creation. The nation is in great difficulty, the people think of authority. Exalting virtue and distinguishing delusion, using ritual to express words. Respectfully presenting fragrant offerings, the palace walls are here. Together awakening the people of heaven, may his spirit come." (26th Special Dispatch)

(Yanzhou) More than twenty people including the national government and various ministry representatives attending the Confucius ceremony, including Chu Minyi, Peng Yangguang, and Wang Yongbin, arrived in Yanzhou at 11:00 AM on the 26th. Li Jingxiu, the adjutant of the 20th Division, was sent to the station to take care of them. After disembarking, the officials went directly to the Railway Hotel designated by the national government to rest. Qiu Wei hosted a lunch banquet at the hotel to entertain Ye Chucang's tour of Mount Tai. The special train returned to Yanzhou at 3:00 PM on the 26th. In addition, all shops and residents in Yancheng hung flags to welcome them. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Yanzhou) Ye Chucang, Chu Minyi, and Fu Rulin are scheduled to visit the Confucius Forest at noon on the 27th and return to Beijing on the Pingpu express train at 3:00 PM that afternoon. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Yanzhou) The Confucius ceremony is scheduled to be held at 7:00 AM on the morning of the 27th at the Confucius Temple in Qufu. The participants will travel by car from Yanzhou at 6:00 AM, first to the Kong Family Mansion in Qielü to rest, and then to the Dacheng Hall of the Confucius Temple to perform the ceremony according to the order stipulated by the central government. After the ceremony, the Kong clan will continue with the family sacrifice. At 1:00 PM, the presiding officers from the national government and various ministries and departments, along with the accompanying officers and the Kong clan, will go to the Confucius Forest to pay respects at the mausoleum, offer wreaths, and perform the ritual in the same order as the sacrificial ceremony, except for the absence of reading the prayer. The sacrificial halls in various places have been decorated separately by the Kong clan on the evening of the 26th. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Zhangjiakou Dispatch: The provincial government's party headquarters has decided to hold a joint memorial week and Confucius sacrifice ceremony on the morning of the 27th. Government offices will be closed, and businesses and residents are ordered to hang flags. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The Confucius sacrifice ceremony in Xuzhou is scheduled to be held at the Red Temple on the morning of the 27th. The chief officiant is Administrative Commissioner Wang Depu. All civil and military government officials and teachers from primary and secondary schools will participate. The ceremony will be solemn, and all sectors will have a day off and hang flags throughout the city to celebrate. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Confucius' Personality and the Spirit of the Age 7

— Shao Yuanchong

(A Work Commemorating Confucius' Birthday)

Recently, the central government advocated cultivating the people's spiritual personality, and thus designated the 27th day of the eighth month, Confucius' birthday, as the Confucius Memorial Day, to promote Confucius' teachings. This is of great importance in correcting the frivolous customs of recent years. According to various accounts of Confucius' birthday, the Gongyang and Guliang Commentaries record it as the gengzi day of the tenth month of the yiyou year, the twenty-first year of Duke Xiang of Lu, which is the twenty-first day of the tenth lunar month. Song Jinglian of the Ming Dynasty advocated this. Huang Lizhou, based on the Zuo Commentary's record that Confucius died on the jichou day of the fourth month in the sixteenth year of Duke Ai, believed that this came from the records of his disciples, and the year and month were no longer doubtful. He also verified it with the Historical Records, Family Sayings, Du Yu's annotations to the Zuo Commentary, and the Ancestral Court Records of the Confucius Family Genealogy, all of which stated that Confucius was seventy-three years old. Therefore, tracing back from the sixteenth year of Duke Ai to the gengxu year, the twenty-second year of Duke Xiang, the beginning of the year matches. The statement in the Confucius Family in the Historical Records that Confucius was born in the twenty-second year of Duke Xiang of Lu should be considered accurate, and Confucius' birth should be estimated as the gengzi day of the eighth month of the yiyou year, the twenty-second year of Duke Xiang, which is the twenty-seventh day of the eighth lunar month, the same as Luo Mi's determination in the History of Roads. The use of the solar calendar now is for convenience.

Confucius' scholarship has encompassed the political thought, ethical philosophy, social morality, and educational principles of China for more than two thousand years, so it is not easy to discuss them all in detail. Moreover, almost all existing Chinese records have been influenced by Confucius' teachings. Discussing it too broadly will inevitably lead to vagueness and aimlessness. Therefore, this article will only discuss aspects that align with the spirit of the age and are sufficient to serve as models for the people's personality, as a source of inspiration. It will strive for breadth and conciseness, and avoid difficulty and obscurity. This is also the humble intention of Jingxian.

(I) The Influence of Confucius' Scholarship and His Place in Chinese National History

Based on historical experience, we firmly believe that any nation that can live and thrive in the world without interruption must have its own history, its own culture, and outstanding figures in its national history. History allows the nation's spirit to be glorified and promoted; culture allows the nation's progress to be expanded and perfected; and outstanding figures in history provide models of personality for the nation, allowing the people to emulate each other and strive for the top, in order to maintain the nation's honor. These three are essential conditions for the nation's spirit. Based on these three to study the history of Confucius, we know that Confucius actually forged these three major conditions for our Chinese nation, leaving them to our descendants, and establishing the great foundation of the Chinese nation. Ancient Chinese culture and scholarship were often scattered and disorganized. Although the Zhou Dynasty rose and the Duke of Zhou established rituals and music, creating a model with brilliant scope, academic books were still stored in government offices and not accessible for private study. It was Confucius who reorganized the classics, taught in person, elaborated and transmitted them, establishing his reputation, and only then did scholarship become accessible to the masses, and national culture flourish, and the work of education spread. Therefore, for more than two thousand years, Confucius has been the only great master in Chinese culture, inheriting the past and ushering in the future. This is his great achievement in national culture. The nation relies on history as the driving force of its spirit. However, ancient history is long and distant, and traditions differ. Confucius revised the Six Classics, using the Spring and Autumn Annals as a record of events, the Book of Rites to record institutions, the Book of Poetry to record folk customs, and the Book of Documents to record proclamations and oaths, all as supplements to history. This is why Zhang Xuecheng had the saying that "all six classics are history," and later historiography flourished, with vast compilations forming a magnificent spectacle for more than two thousand years. Although their style was not entirely refined and their observation of social changes was relatively limited, they have been unmatched by the historical departments of any country in the world, and their impact on national observation and gradual immersion in awakening the national spirit is immense. This is Confucius' contribution to national history. As for Confucius' own place in history, he is actually one of the three founders of the Chinese nation. The three founders are: the Yellow Emperor Xuanyuan, who pioneered the wilderness, expanded the territory, and first laid the foundation for China, leaving it to our descendants for billions of years without end, and is truly the ancestor of the nation's founding; during the time of Yao and Shun, floods were rampant, and the people's livelihood deteriorated, but Yu the Great worked hard for thirteen years, controlling the waters, dredging the rivers, and then the people were able to live in peace, and agriculture prospered, benefiting the people's livelihood and making meritorious contributions for all ages; Confucius followed Yao and Shun, modeled himself on Wen and Wu, widely consulted various opinions, edited the Book of Poetry and the Book of Documents, established the Book of Rites and the Book of Music, traveled through various countries, promoted the learning of governing the world, lectured and taught, with three thousand disciples, seventy-two of whom were proficient in the Six Arts, carrying on the past and opening up the future, continuing the interrupted careers of past sages, gathering the great achievements of scholarship, and becoming a model for all ages. These three founders either created the foundation of the nation, or benefited the people's livelihood with universal benefit, or were the masters of culture, all opening up a hundred generations to come, allowing our Chinese nation to stand tall on the earth, continuously and endlessly, shining brightly without limit. With these three founders as models in front, sages and virtuous men have risen up, one after another, and academic achievements and careers have flourished in a hundred ways, and our Chinese history is therefore brilliant on the earth, encouraging our nation to work diligently and forge ahead, cultivating the national spirit and increasing its self-confidence. Confucius' teaching and training, and his personality of enriching and shining by embodying himself, are truly the greatest foundation of our Chinese nation's spirit.

Confucius was a practical educator, and also a political scientist and philosopher. In any aspect, he was able to express his great spirit. Therefore, Confucius' learning can be applied to action everywhere, from the inside to the outside, extending from oneself to others, encompassing both the root and the branch, and uniting theory and practice. Therefore, what he taught was the learning of governing the world and engaging in politics, and what he learned was the way to understand principles and achieve practical application. He wanted to turn chaos into order, move from a state of modest comfort to one of prosperity, and ultimately to achieve great peace. Therefore, he said, "I would rather entrust it to practical action than to empty words." This is the meaning of knowing and then acting. In his teaching, the way of learning is to start with broad learning and then inquire carefully, to think cautiously and discern clearly, and only when one is absolutely certain and without doubt does one then return to diligent practice. This is the meaning of learning and then striving for practical application. The order of cultivating oneself and governing others is to start with investigating things to understand principles, extending knowledge to study and explore the essence, making one's intentions sincere to screen out external desires, rectifying one's heart to correct one's direction, and cultivating oneself to establish one's personality. This is the work of cultivating oneself. Once the work of cultivating oneself is established, then one is close enough to manage one's family, great enough to govern the country, and even more so to bring peace to the world. This is the effect of governing others. If the work of cultivating oneself cannot be practiced diligently and achieved deeply, then virtue is not enough to convince people, and talent is not enough to be constant and adapt to change, and one can never achieve the effect of governing others. If the effect of governing others is not evident, then it can prove that the work of cultivating oneself is not yet complete. This is also a discussion of the connection between the root and the branch. Therefore, when speaking of wisdom and virtue, he emphasized dual cultivation; when speaking of knowledge and action, he emphasized parallel advancement; and when speaking of politics and education, he emphasized consistency. He sought to have everyone hone their personality, be diligent in their practice, enrich their intelligence, and strive for the distant and great, for learning that is substantial and useful, and to maximize the work of cultivating oneself and governing others. His breadth and depth are truly sufficient to enlighten later generations endlessly.

However, although Confucius' scholarship is so diligent and substantial, for more than two thousand years, due to the fact that monarchs of various dynasties selected Confucius' sayings about respecting the monarch, interpreting them out of context, and vigorously advocating anything that was conducive to consolidating monarchical power, while other subtle words and great meanings were buried and not made manifest. This is one of the misfortunes of Confucius' scholarship. Generations of scholars devoted themselves to the study of chapters and verses, textual research, and empty theories of morality, burying themselves in old papers, and forgetting to return home until their hair turned white. Broadly speaking, there was the learning of commentary and exegesis in the Han Dynasty, and the learning of moral principles in the Song Dynasty, each exalting itself and attacking different schools. During the Ming and Qing dynasties, the disputes between the Han and Song schools became divided, with clear-cut camps, each believing that they had obtained the true transmission of Confucius' learning, and even using the principles of Buddhism and Taoism to deduce the meaning of the classics, discussing metaphysics and practicing stillness, becoming increasingly empty. In fact, language and words were definitely not Confucius' meaning of practice, and maintaining emptiness and guarding stillness were even more contrary to Confucius' admonition of diligent practice. Therefore, the more scholars who discussed and wrote, the more obscure the true meaning of Confucius' learning became, and the constant principles could not regulate the people's ethics, and the changes could not save the country from disaster. Those who pursued careers then criticized Confucius' learning as empty and useless, but they did not know that scholars of chapters and verses were not sufficient to represent Confucius' learning. This is another misfortune of Confucius' learning. Since the opening of the seas, European and American politics, education, and scholarship have gradually spread to the East, and the Chinese people, shocked by their rich and powerful practical effects, have completely followed what they have learned and learned it. Therefore, they especially blamed Confucius' learning, or even created the saying that Chinese characters could be abolished and all thread-bound books could be discarded. This is another misfortune of Confucius' learning. How can they know that the reason why Confucius' learning is not manifest is that the blame lies with those scholars who are constrained by chapters and verses and use empty theories to confuse the truth of Confucius' learning. The development of a nation's character must rely on the cultivation of the nation's history and cultural spirit in order to maintain the nation without decay. Therefore, Sun Yat-sen, with his innate talent, deeply studied and widely consulted, swept away all the obstacles of Confucius' learning, promoted the lost learning, and understood the root cause. Only then was the true scholarship of Confucius able to be revealed to our nation in a clear and open way after two thousand years of hardship and distress. From now on, we should continue to inherit the subtle words, revive the fallen threads, to clarify the reality of theory and practice, diligently practice our accomplishments, establish the spirit of ambition and perseverance, reach the realm of high intelligence, promote universal relief in times of difficulty, and turn chaos into order. The people should strive together.

(II) Confucius' View of Personality

Confucius' personality is seen in his cultivation and learning, in his teaching, and in his handling of affairs. In his self-description of cultivation and learning, he started with "at fifteen, I set my heart on learning" and continued until "at seventy, I could follow what my heart desired, without transgressing the line." In these decades, he never stopped working hard to cultivate himself. Therefore, he described himself as "He is the kind of person who forgets to eat when he is determined, forgets his worries when he is happy, and does not know that old age is coming," and also said, "Learning without being tired." This proves his joy in learning and his ability to gain something from it. In his teaching, he "teaches without being weary," "teaches without discrimination," and "guides people step by step." He also feared that teaching would be too easy and that students would take it lightly, so he treated them with the way of "I do not enlighten those who are not eager to learn, nor do I explain to those who are not anxious to understand. If I raise one corner and they cannot return with the other three, I do not repeat myself," so that students can cultivate themselves diligently and achieve deep understanding on their own. He encouraged students to be diligent and unremitting, such as telling Zigong the meaning of never resting in life (Confucius's Heavenly Omen), and deeply admonishing his disciples to "plan for the Way, not for food; worry about the Way, not about poverty," and "do not worry about not having a position, worry about what to establish," and the nones of "longing for home" and "being ashamed of wearing poor clothes and eating poor food" are all deeply clear and insightful arguments. As for the weight of his own responsibility and the courage of his self-confidence, he described himself as saying, "If someone were to use me, it would be enough in a month, and there would be achievements in three years," and after being the prime minister of Lu for three months, he achieved the practical effect of "men and women walking separately on the road, not picking up lost items, men valuing loyalty and trustworthiness, women valuing chastity and obedience, and guests from all directions feeling at home," and at the meeting at Jiagu, he dressed in ceremonial robes to intimidate Qi, and when he destroyed the three capitals, the power of the strong vassals was weakened. All of this was done with unwavering devotion and upright conduct, so he was able to influence others, and the powerful and strong would collapse on their own, unlike those who could talk but could not act. Moreover, the order of his measures was always to exhaust himself in loyalty and reciprocity, and to practice himself and extend it to things, so he "established himself to establish others, and achieved himself to achieve others." Even when he was in a difficult situation, at a time when petty people were obstructing him, he still held the spirit of "knowing that it cannot be done and doing it anyway" to take on the heavy responsibility of the world. How could the scholars of chapters and verses in later generations be able to look up to even a fraction of it?

Confucius' diligent and glorious personality was created by his broad and extensive learning, and the reason why Confucius' learning was achieved was that he was able to seek teachers and friends widely and consult and survey extensively. Therefore, Zigong praised him, saying, "The Master learns everywhere, and from whom does he constantly learn?" This means that Confucius' learning has no constant teacher. Therefore, he asked Lao Dan and Shan Zi about rituals, Chang Hong about music (Book of Rites, Record of Music), and Shi Xiangzi about playing the qin (Han Poetry, Outer Biography). He obtained the Book of Changes and the Spring and Autumn Annals from the Grand Historian of Lu, and Guan Bai Er Guo Bao Shu, like Zuo Qiuming of Zhou. His learning was extremely broad. Among his teachers and friends, there were those mentioned in the Historical Records, "He sought advice from Laozi in Zhou, Qu Boyu in Wei, Yan Pingzhong in Qi, Laizi in Chu, Zichan in Zheng, and Meng Gongchuo in Lu. He often mentioned Zang Wenzhong, Liu Xiahui, Tong Ti Bohua, and Jieshanzi, but Confucius was always behind them and not in the same generation." Because his observation was broad, he was able to develop great ideas and compile the sayings of the masses, and his seventy-two worthy disciples were all talented men of the time, each striving in what they had learned to enhance and broaden the master's teachings. This is why, while there were hundreds of schools contending in Confucius' time, after the change of dynasties, most of them declined and disappeared, while Confucius' learning became increasingly glorious, like a river gathering thousands of tributaries to become the sea, what it takes is broad, and what it achieves is great, unlike shallow streams, which dry up in no time.

Therefore, those who want to emulate Confucius' personality must emulate his lifelong love of learning and his tireless diligence, must emulate his tireless teaching and his teaching without discrimination, must emulate his combined use of theory and practice and his consistent conduct, must emulate his taking on the heavy responsibility of the world and his knowing that it cannot be done and doing it anyway, must emulate his restoring discipline and綱and his tearing down powerful tyrants and 理and his rebuking strong neighbors, and must emulate his consulting and surveying widely and his seeking teachers and friends extensively. Emptying his heart to seek knowledge and diligently practicing to take on responsibility, this is being a good student.

(III) Confucius' Teachings and the Spirit of the Age

The essence of Confucius' teachings lies in reorganizing ancient scholarship and culture, and developing and expanding it to later generations. The Six Classics speak of this in detail. What we should especially draw from his life and teachings today as a source of inspiration and encouragement is his great righteousness of expelling the barbarians and avenging wrongs, his theory of people's livelihood, and his doctrine of universal love. Keeping the Chinese people within the Chinese nation and keeping the barbarians outside has always been the foundation of the Chinese national spirit. The writing style of the Spring and Autumn Annals not only disparaged the barbarians, but also regarded those who were originally descendants of the Yellow Emperor but had the behavior of barbarians as barbarians. Those who were not of our race were especially placed in the category of exclusion. Therefore, the Confucian school may have criticized Guan Zhong's contribution to assisting Qi as being mixed with hegemonism, but Confucius praised him, saying, "Guan Zhong rectified the world, and the people still benefit from it today. Without Guan Zhong, we would be wearing our hair loose and buttoning our clothes on the left." He approved of him as being benevolent. The Zuo Commentary mentions the saving of the condemned by the people of Qi, saying, "The Rong and Di are like jackals and wolves, and cannot be satisfied. The Xia are close and intimate, and cannot be abandoned." This interpretation of the meaning of expelling the barbarians is truly able to understand Confucius' teachings. Later, Hu Anguo, living in the late Song Dynasty, when the northern barbarians invaded and the country was almost not a country, wrote the Spring and Autumn Annals to express his righteousness of expelling the barbarians and avenging wrongs. These were all able to inherit Confucius' teachings of the Spring and Autumn Annals to develop the great righteousness of the nation and extend the supreme teachings of expelling the barbarians. As for the righteousness of revenge, even though Duke Xiang of Qi was not virtuous, the Spring and Autumn Annals still praised his ability to avenge the wrongs of nine generations and concealed his responsibility for destroying Ji. The Gongyang school extended this saying, believing that revenge was permissible even after a hundred generations. This is the righteousness of avenging national wrongs. Sheng of the Song Dynasty also said, "Whether or not revenge should be taken does not depend solely on the distance of years and the change of dynasties, but is determined by the depth of the wrong. If someone destroys our country, cuts off our ancestral sacrifices, we suddenly abandon what gods and men both hate, and we must take revenge even after a hundred generations, as Song did against Jin." Peng Jiaping also said, "According to the Book of Rites, one should not live under the same sky with the enemy of one's father. According to the Tan Gong, Confucius answered Zixia's question about living with the enemy of one's parents by telling him not to live under the same sky with him, and if they meet in the marketplace, they should fight without turning back." This is also an extension of the meaning of revenge. As for his teachings of "behaving with shame" and "national shame is enough to revive the country," they are especially sufficient to greatly promote the righteousness of understanding shame and are what those who are determined to avenge national wrongs must repeatedly consider and pay attention to. Therefore, if we can constantly encourage ourselves with Confucius' great righteousness of expelling the barbarians and avenging wrongs, then no matter what strong enemy or foreign trouble inflicts us with aggression, our nation will be able to unite as one, unyielding and indomitable, and strive with all our might to avenge the national wrongs together. This is truly the essence of the national spirit, and it is this spirit that has encouraged patriotic people for thousands of years to follow one after another, to cut off their heads and tear their chests to defend the country and protect the race, even if they die nine times without regret. If the Chinese nation wants to survive on the earth, it must use Confucius' great righteousness of expelling the barbarians and avenging wrongs to admonish themselves daily, fathers instructing their sons, brothers warning their younger brothers, husbands encouraging their wives, and elders exhorting the young, in order to promote this righteousness of the nation.

As for Confucius' emphasis on people's livelihood, such as when he first served as the magistrate of Zhongdu, he established rules for nourishing the living and sending off the dead (Family Sayings). In his Analects, when discussing the policies of the two emperors and three kings, he specifically mentioned their words emphasizing the people's food, funerals, and sacrifices. Food nourishes life, while funerals and sacrifices send off the dead, which are truly the foundation of China's people's livelihood politics. When Confucius answered Zigong's question about governance, he prioritized having sufficient food before having sufficient soldiers. When he answered Ran You, he regarded the three things of abundance, wealth, and education as the major principles of governing the country. When he answered Zizhang, he regarded benefiting the people's interests as the essential meaning of engaging in politics. These are all refined and subtle arguments for considering the people's livelihood. The mutual use of the three meanings of abundance, wealth, and education is truly where the essence of national construction lies. Without abundance, there is no way to deeply plant its foundation; without wealth, there is no way to perfect its life; and without education, there is no way to promote its progress. With the three meanings presented together, the politics of people's livelihood are full and without omissions. The phrase "benefiting the people's interests" is especially the foundation of governance. If what the people desire is followed, and what the people hate is removed, then the people can each fulfill their lives, and the foundation of peace and order will be established. The highest principle of modern politics is nothing more than this. How can those who govern not embody and diligently practice it?

Confucius' meaning of universal love has been expressed completely in the two words "benevolence" and "reciprocity." Benevolence is to love people, and loving people must mean thinking about how to benefit them. Thinking about how to love people must mean being able to share the people's likes and dislikes. Thinking about how to benefit people must mean liking what the people like and disliking what the people dislike. Extending this meaning, people must be able to fulfill the reality of mutual assistance, and those who govern must be able to fulfill the sincerity of loving the people. If others have pain and suffering, it is as if one has it oneself. Wherever interests lie, there is no distinction between oneself and others. This is what is called universal love, which is also the original meaning of universal love. As for the meaning of reciprocity, it lies in extending from oneself to others. Therefore, if one thinks of peace, one would never bear to place others in danger; if one thinks of joy, one would never bear to force others into suffering; if one thinks of avoiding harm, one would never be able to inflict harm on others; if one thinks of pursuing benefit, one would never be able to monopolize the benefit for oneself. From this, one can further extend it to "respecting one's elders as one respects one's own elders, and caring for one's young as one cares for one's own young," and to what Mencius said, "Goods and beautiful women should be shared with the people," which does not harm benevolent governance. One should strive to avoid the bravery of a single individual and seek to be the great brave who conquers cruelty and eliminates killing and punishes the violent and pacifies the good. One husband and one wife in Yi Yin's country are not benefited by his grace, as if he himself had pushed them into a harmful harvest trap. Even further, the spirit of "if the people are hungry, it is as if he himself is hungry; if the people are drowning, it is as if he himself is drowning" is sufficient to express Confucius' meaning of universal love. Benevolence and reciprocity should be used together. Without benevolence, there is no reciprocity; without reciprocity, the effect of benevolence cannot be fully realized. Benevolence and reciprocity, the meaning of universal love is complete and without regret. Moreover, the meaning of reciprocity is not only limited to what is called "do not do to others what you do not want done to yourself," but should also be expanded to "do to others what you want done to yourself." In this way, the meaning of extending from oneself to others, mutual benefit and mutual assistance becomes clearer, and the meaning of the Great Harmony in the Book of Rites is manifested. Confucius' refined principles of universal love are comprehensive and without regret.

(IV) The Future of Confucius' Teachings and Chinese Culture

From the above-mentioned meanings, we are already aware of the breadth and depth of Confucius' teachings and their relevance to the direction of modern national efforts. We know that it is definitely not as the frivolous and superficial people who do not read books imagine, thinking that Confucius' learning is completely contrary to the modern era and should be completely discarded. Therefore, if our nation wants to strive with hard work to fight for survival, to restore the glory of its past, and to illuminate the light of our nation's history, it must be necessary to study Confucius' teachings. Any nation that can independently survive on the earth must have its own history and culture, thereby increasing its national self-confidence and its courage to fight. From this, it will promote and develop its inherent culture, and then its national progress will be limitless. Although any nation cannot but vigorously pursue the culture of the era in order to adapt to the times, the culture of the era must be based on the culture of history, and the spirit of the era must also be based on the spirit of history. Otherwise, it will be like water without a source and a tree without roots, and it will never be able to develop fundamentally. Therefore, no matter how vigorously China's contemporary culture pursues the upstream, it cannot but take Confucius' teachings, which gather the great achievements of ancient historical culture, as the foundation of the new culture. Today, the invaders are deep. If we want to express the nation's divine bravery in defending the country, we must express our inherent national spirit. The driving force of the national spirit must lie in the nation's inherent historical culture and its model figures in history. Then, who should we turn to other than Confucius? Who should we turn to other than the model of Confucius' personality? To summarize Confucius' teachings that are suitable for the spirit of the age, in governance, we should express his firmness, his sense of responsibility, and the essential meaning of his benevolence towards the people, his love of things, and his great benefit to the people's livelihood. In resisting insults, we should express his spirit of expelling the barbarians and avenging wrongs and understanding shame.

Confucius Stone Statue (in Zhong County, Sichuan) 8

It is rare to see a complete Confucius stone statue. This statue was created in the third year of Shaosheng in the Song Dynasty. It is exquisitely carved, and its expression is complete. It was buried for a long time in the wilderness outside the north city of Zhong County, Sichuan. The people of the county obtained it and established a school palace. It was not until the late Qing Dynasty that it was transplanted to the new Confucius Temple outside the city. Recently, Qin Yuepu, the director of the Finance Section of Zhong County, took a picture of it and sent it as a gift to this newspaper.

Page 4

The Eastern Route Army Recovers Muyang 9

Navy Sends Ships to Blockade the Harbor

(Fuzhou) After a fierce crackdown, the remnants of Luo Binghui and Fang Zhimin scattered and hid in remote places to heal their wounds. One part sneaked into Muyang, stubbornly resisting by the river. At twelve o'clock on the night of the twenty-third, our Wu Chengren's division attacked across the river by torchlight. After three hours of fierce fighting, the bandits were defeated, and many bandits and firearms were captured. On the morning of the twenty-fourth, our army completely recovered Muyang and rushed to deal with the aftermath. The bandits fled north towards Fuan, and our Wu Chen and other divisions have been tracking and pursuing them, and have telegraphed the Zhejiang Security Team to block and suppress them. In order to suppress the scattered bandits in eastern Fujian, the provincial authorities ordered the various departments of Wu Chen Wang to cooperate with the Zhejiang Air Force to follow and suppress them according to the predetermined plan, and to eliminate them within a time limit. The Navy has sent four more warships to open fire and suppress them in eastern Fujian, and has strictly blockaded the harbor to cut off supplies to the bandits. The county magistrate of Ningyang telegraphed the province to report that the bandits who had fled from the Qinggui area were engaged in fierce battles with our army for days. Our army advanced in three routes to encircle and attack them. The bandits in Hongshakou, Shifeng, Guzhu and other places were all defeated in a panic. (Central News Agency telegram on the 26th)

(Fuzhou) A certain division telegraphed the province, saying that on the twenty-fourth, the division captured Muyuan. The Fang Luo bandits resisted by the river. After three hours of courageous attack, they defeated the bandits and captured many of them. They are now pursuing them northwest towards Fuan. Another message said that the bandits, due to the close pursuit of our army, have turned to Shouning. The provincial authorities immediately ordered a certain division commander to lead two regiments to be stationed in Shouning, and to invite the Security Team to advance in a joint encirclement, so as to annihilate them as soon as possible. (Special telegram on the 26th)

(Xiamen) Zhangzhou news, the pseudo-Third Army Corps attacked Liancheng with thousands of men. They did not succeed and retreated thirty miles from the city, disturbing the countryside in separate groups. They were also defeated by the national army on the left and right wings. Refugees have returned to their homes one after another. (Special telegram on the 26th)

The Yellow River's Water Level Stops Rising 10

The South Canal Rises Greatly

(Tianjin) The Yellow River's water level has stopped rising, and the flow is very slow. The project to close all the openings is in progress. (Special telegram on the 26th)

(Tianjin) The water in the South Canal has risen greatly. The Qihe Dam, which is twenty miles east of Qing County, has been breached by three feet and six inches. In addition, the Dou Di Jianhe Sluice has been washed away by the current. The River Bureau is currently supervising the construction and stacking 83 sacks of hemp to rush the blockade. Lin Chengxiu, the director of the Hebei Construction Department, telegraphed the province to report today. (Special telegram on the 26th)

There Is Rain in the Yangtze River Area 11

(Wuxi) There was heavy rain at 7:00 pm today. The water level in the river suddenly dropped by two inches this morning, and then rose by two inches after the rain. (Special telegram on the 26th)

(Nanjing) Nanjing was still hot on the twenty-sixth, with a temperature of 95 degrees in the morning. There was heavy rain at about 4:00 pm, which did not stop until evening. The temperature has been reduced to 73 degrees, and the climate has turned cool. (Central News Agency telegram on the 26th)

(Hankou) Hankou has been hot for a month. There was a shower at 11:00 am on the twenty-sixth, which stopped after ten minutes. The climate was slightly cooler, but it was of no help to the crops. (Central News Agency telegram on the 26th)

(Zhenjiang) Zhenjiang is still as hot as midsummer after entering autumn. There was heavy rain in the afternoon of the twenty-sixth, which did not stop until evening. The rainfall has reached about four inches. The water in the low-lying streets is knee-deep, and the climate has turned cool. (Special telegram on the 26th)

Korean Drug Trafficking Organization

(Tianjin) Tong County telephone, on the morning of the twenty-fifth, the Public Security Bureau captured a Korean drug trafficking organization. The police arrested the Korean, and several Koreans resisted with weapons, but were eventually captured. Outside the South Gate of Shanhaiguan 13

Police Repel Bandits

(Tianjin) A gang of bandits is hiding outside the South Gate of Shanhaiguan, with complete firearms. During the day on the twenty-fifth, Guan Desheng, a clerk in a Western clothing store, went to the Xiaomubiao Bridge south of the railway due to an incident. More than a dozen bandits suddenly came and forced Guan to flee to the northwest. The Public Security Bureau heard the news and pursued them. A fierce battle broke out in the nearby cemetery outside the gate. After about two hours, the bandits were unable to hold on and fled after abandoning their tickets. (Special telegram on the 26th)

Three Loan Items of the Ministry of Railways 14

Gu Mengyu Negotiates Separately in Peiping

(Peiping) Gu Mengyu has been in Peiping for nearly a month, conducting loan negotiations and summoning bureau directors from various routes to Peiping to discuss business reorganization. The main loan items total three: (1) The Peiping-Hankow Railway reorganization loan, totaling 30 million, of which 15 million will be used to build the Yellow River Railway Bridge, and the remaining funds will be used to purchase materials and vehicles. This item is being negotiated with domestic banking groups. (2) The Peiping-Suiyuan Railway realignment loan is already showing promising signs and should be resolved within about a week. (3) The Baoning Line construction loan. The Ministry of Railways has long had plans to build the Baotou-Ningxia Railway. If the loan is successful, technicians will be sent to conduct surveys. Gu is determined to resolve all of the above items one by one before leaving Peiping. After leaving Peiping, he will first go to Qingdao and Jinan to inspect railway affairs. The bureau directors from various routes who have been summoned to Peiping in recent days include Qian Zongze, Director of the Longhai Railway Bureau, Xu Wenguo, Deputy Director of the Peiping-Ningbo Railway, Ge Guangting, Commissioner of the Jiaoji Railway, Chen Yanjiong, Commissioner of the Peiping-Hankow Railway, and Shen Chang, Director of the Peiping-Suiyuan Railway. Gu has been summoning them for talks in recent days, and the content is very confidential. (26th Special Dispatch)

Ten Provinces' Anti-Smoking Affairs 16

Temporarily Handled by the Military Council

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Municipal Government received an order from Chairman Chiang of the Military Council, which was issued by the National Government, stating that anti-smoking matters in the ten provinces of Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Shaanxi, and Gansu will be temporarily handled by the Military Council during the bandit suppression period. All provinces and cities must enforce military orders and military law regarding smoking bans in order to eradicate the accumulated problems of past years. The Municipal Government immediately ordered all subordinates to comply. (26th Special Dispatch)

Economic Council Sends Personnel 17

To Inspect Water Conservancy in Jiangxi Province

(Nanjing) Kong Xiangxi believes that Jiangxi has suffered from banditry for many years, and this year it is also facing a drought. He has telegraphed the Economic Council from Shanghai to send personnel to Jiangxi to inspect water conservancy, so as to benefit farmland irrigation and alleviate the people's difficulties. The council has now dispatched Lin Youlong to depart immediately to go together with the council's office in Jiangxi to handle water conservancy for the entire province. Peiping-Suiyuan Railway 18

Transportation Returns to Original State

(Peiping) Transportation on the Peiping-Suiyuan Railway has returned to its original state. Although the railway tracks washed away by floods at eighteen locations have been repaired, the realignment work has not changed. The survey team will return next week. After the Peiping-Suiyuan Railway route map is drawn, it will be submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval and handling in order to begin construction. If the railway tracks are realigned, it is hoped that Peiping-Suiyuan Railway transportation will no longer be affected by floods. (26th Special Dispatch)

Zhejiang Province Receives Order 19

To Establish Security Command Headquarters

Commander to be Concurrently Held by Chairman

Security Department Also Under Control

(Hangzhou) Zhejiang Province has received an order to establish a provincial security command headquarters. The position of commander will be concurrently held by the chairman of the provincial government and will be the highest military commander in the province. The headquarters organization has now been determined and will be established soon. After the headquarters is established, the Security Department will also be under its control. Due to financial difficulties, the current Security Department has decided to implement austerity measures and lay off staff. The original five sections have been reduced to four. It is also heard that the Security Department may add one deputy director. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Zhejiang Levies Transportation Surtax 20

(Hangzhou) The Zhejiang Relief Association, following the precedent of the 18th year of the Republic, plans to continue levying a transportation surtax from October 1st of this year. The railway will be taxed at 1%, and steamships and automobiles will be taxed at 0.5%, temporarily for a period of one year. It has been submitted to the provincial government for forwarding to the Ministry of Transportation. (26th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Kong Xiangxi Invites Xiao Chunjin for Talks 21

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi is in Jiangxi. Due to the severe drought in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, which has not been seen in sixty years, thorough improvements in water conservancy are urgently needed. He invited Xiao Chunjin to consult on everything. After Xiao provided detailed opinions on water conservancy, he also reported that the rivers in Jiangxi Province have been silted up for many years. If they are not dredged, droughts will inevitably occur after a year. Kong then telegraphed the Economic Council to send personnel to Jiangxi for surveying. The council dispatched Lin Youlong, section chief of the Engineering Section of the Water Conservancy Department, who took a ship to Jiangxi on the 26th. (26th Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Revises 27

Measures for Collecting Mineral Resource Tax

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance is revising the measures for collecting mineral resource taxes to reorganize the tax revenue. (1) Following the cotton spinning consolidated tax method, the tax will be based on the selling price of the goods, and the quality will be distinguished into several grades. (2) Following the cigarette consolidated tax, a method combining ad valorem and ad valorem taxes will be determined, such as classifying the price per ton into a first grade for prices above a certain amount and a second grade for prices below a certain amount, with a fixed tax amount for each grade. After consulting with the Ministry of Industry, it will be presented to the Executive Yuan for forwarding to the Legislative Yuan for review and implementation. (26th Special Dispatch)

Japanese and Puppets Transport 54

Drugs Into the Pass from Yu and Re

=Opium Tax Collection Agencies Widely Established in Yu and Re=

=Tax Revenue This Autumn May Reach Over 30 Million=

=Japanese Issue Fumin Lottery in Northeast=

Chengde Communication: Agriculture in Rehe has always been dominated by opium cultivation. Now, at the time of opium harvest, large quantities of black goods are being transported from Rehe to various places. The quantity entering the Great Wall passes to Hebei, Chahar, and Shandong is particularly large. Also, the Puppet State Council previously sent personnel to Yuguan to investigate the sales of drugs there. As a result, it was deemed necessary to establish an office of the Opium Monopoly Office. As a result, houses have been found in Dongluocheng and will be established soon and start working.

Since the Japanese imitated our Aviation Lottery and issued the "Fumin Lottery" in the Northeast, many people have been deceived. The business of the so-called "Fumin Lottery Selling Point" in major cities and towns in the Northeast is very widespread and has become very developed. It is heard that business has already begun.

German Newspaper Discusses Far East Situation 55

Japan and Russia Are Only Posturing

Negotiations on Buying the Road Have Room for Reconciliation

War Avoidable for the Time Being Due to Economic Relations

(Berlin) German newspapers are still paying close attention to the situation in the Far East. Several newspapers have published pessimistic news about Japanese-Russian relations. The Attack Newspaper said, "Although the situation between the two countries is like this, they will exhaust their diplomatic intelligence to avoid a break before a final split. It is not credible that they will suddenly have a conflict. Sending troops is indeed a show of threat, but its nature is still only a 'show.' Moreover, the major powers have not clearly defined their attitudes, so there is still room for bargaining and reconciliation between Japan and Russia." The Political Foreign Affairs Correspondence newspaper said that the alarming news published by the newspapers has caused many countries to worry. The China Eastern Railway has become a formal issue for discussion between Moscow and Tokyo. In fact, the price demanded by the Russian side is very close to the price returned by "Manchukuo" and Japan. If both sides are sincere, it will not be difficult to reach a compromise. The difference between them is only a few million yuan. Can they go to war for this small amount? In addition to this, there are other factors that make war difficult to occur. For example, Soviet Russia is experiencing difficulties both domestically and abroad. Although it has reconciled with France, it will not help the Manchurian battlefield. As for Japan, it is striving for economic development. The outbreak of war would be sufficient to hinder economic development due to the need for raw materials. Therefore, both are unfavorable for a war. Therefore, the conclusion of the Foreign Affairs Correspondence newspaper is that Germans all hope that the conflict in the Far East will not exceed newspaper debates and the exchange of diplomatic documents. (25th Havas Dispatch)

Washington Insiders Observe 56

Japan-Russia War Machine Is Imminent

(Washington) According to the intentions of senior government officials and experienced international observers, the tense situation between Japan and Russia caused by "Manchukuo" has reached a dangerous level. Important aspects here all express serious doubts, fearing that there will be an explosive event in "Manchukuo" that will plunge Japan and Russia into a war vortex. These observers all believe that the two countries do not want to fight at this time, but if an unexpected event occurs, neither country will be willing to give in and lose "face", then war will break out. As for the issue of the price of the China Eastern Railway, which Japan and Russia are fighting over, the difference is only 40 million Japanese yen, which can only be used for one day's expenses if Japan and Russia go to war. However, the leaders of the two countries will not take this into account and would rather risk the danger of war. The US military authorities believe that as winter approaches, both sides have large-scale troop movements, and the war machine is approaching day by day. (25th National Dispatch)

Soviet Russia 57

Makes Great Efforts to Contact Outer Mongolia

Russian Personnel Serve as Technical Advisors to the Mongolian Army

A Form of Anti-Japanese Alliance by the British and American Navies Has Been Formed

(Moscow) There are two important indications in the thinking of the Soviet Russian newspapers on the Far East issue today. First, Soviet Russia believes that the three major naval powers cannot agree to the extension of the Washington and London treaties due to Japan's new position in the Pacific. Second, Soviet Russia clearly wants to establish the most friendly relations with the "Outer Mongolian Republic," because military experts all say that if the Japanese army wants to attack Soviet Russia, it must first pass through Outer Mongolia. The Communist Party's organ newspaper Pravda commented that the first phase of the naval talks has failed, largely because Japan is unwilling to discuss political issues at next year's naval conference and declares that it demands recognition of Japan's special position in the Pacific. Now, the naval countries have planned to greatly expand their navies. The only result is nothing more than the United Kingdom and the United States taking unified action on Japan's position in the Far East. Therefore, the fate of the naval conference has been decided, and the naval countries' struggle for dominance cannot be avoided. At the same time, a telegram from Outer Mongolia stated the actions of the Soviet delegation Garakhan and others at the tenth anniversary of the "Outer Mongolian Republic." In addition to sending many gifts, such as airplanes and cars, Garakhan also congratulated Outer Mongolia on its progress in the economic and cultural fields and the achievements of the Mongolian Red Army. It is said that there are Soviet Russian personnel serving as technical advisors in the Mongolian army. (26th National News Agency Dispatch)

Arrested Russian Personnel 58

Have Reached Eighty One After Another

Subjected to Flogging and Abuse

Russia Lodges a Serious Protest

(Harbin) The conspiracy to subvert the Eastern Route train was exposed on the 13th and 14th, and many Soviet employees were reported. As of the 25th, the number of suspects arrested reached 70 or 80. (26th Japan Allied Dispatch)

Russian Protest 59

Japanese Military Department Ignores It

(Tokyo) Since the Soviet Union did not approve of Foreign Minister Hirota's good intentions of mediation, it took advantage of the crisis of the breakdown of the Eastern Route transfer issue to launch its blatant anti-Japanese propaganda tactics. The Japanese side had no choice but to publish the entire process of the negotiations on the 22nd to correct the Soviet side's errors. However, during this period, the Soviet Union incited its bureau employees to repeatedly obstruct the train operations, subvert trains, and frequently engage in anti-Manchu and anti-Japanese conspiracies. Therefore, the "Manchukuo" government arrested its unruly elements, which is the so-called arrest of Eastern Route Russian employees. However, regarding this case, a certain Soviet Russian consul stationed in Manchuria lodged a provocative protest to the Kwantung Army Special Service Agency on August 15, saying that the issue of arresting Eastern Route employees was not to promote the Soviet Union's sale of the Eastern Route, but to attempt to increase troops in the Far East. The Japanese army completely disregarded the above protest and immediately ignored it. However, the general public believes that it is worrying that such frequent demonstrations and propaganda will continue in the future, and attention should be paid to its future. (26th Japan Allied Dispatch)

(Changchun) The Sino-Manchukuo waterway conference has largely completed the review of the agreed-upon text and will be formally signed this month. Now they have been forced to cede their houses, and the tragic situation is unbearable to watch. (26th Hualian Dispatch)

Japanese Ministry of Communications 66

Plans to Establish an Aviation Network

Emphasis on Liaison Between Civilian and Military Affairs

Completed in Two Phases on a Large Scale

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Communications has been vigorously studying the expansion of civil aviation as part of its national policy. It has now drafted a general outline for expanding aviation and will soon submit the plan to the Army and Navy. The main points of the outline will focus on civil aviation while organically integrating it with the Army and Navy aviation, linking transportation aviation with national defense aviation. The total cost of the first phase of the plan is approximately 20 million yen, with over 2.8 million yen for the first year already included in the next year's budget proposal and submitted to the Ministry of Finance. The second phase of the plan aims to counter the regular air routes opened to the Orient by European countries and the advancement of the Soviet Union and the United States in the North Pacific. It also includes the circular air routes for important Japanese cities, requiring a cost of over 100 million yen. The scale is extremely broad and immense. The details of the two phases of the plan are as follows:

"Phase 1" Regular air routes between Japan and Taiwan, regular air routes between Japan and the South Seas, regular air routes between Tokyo and Sapporo, regular connecting air routes between Osaka, Tokushima, and Kochi, the Osaka-Matsue connecting route, the Osaka-Fuji-Nagano connecting route, and the Tokyo-Nagano-Niigata route.

"Phase 2" New routes must be established between Taiwan and the South Seas, the Sapporo-Sakhalin route, the Kanto-Tohoku circular route, the Hokuriku-Sanin route, the Tokai-Sanyo route, and the Kyushu circular route. (26th Japanese Allied Press Telegram)

Problem of Abolishing the Naval Treaty 67

Japan Studies Carefully

Early Notification May Provoke Negative Reactions from Britain and the United States

Navy Advocates Adapting to Circumstances After the Preparatory Conference

(Tokyo) Regarding the issue of abolishing the Washington Naval Treaty, internal opinions within the government have become consistent. However, there is still room for study regarding the timing and procedures. The Bureau of Legislation and the Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Navy are carefully conducting research. The countermeasures for arms reduction in the Navy will be submitted to the Cabinet Council in early next month at the same time. Regarding the timing of the abolition notification, the Navy believes that if it is done before the preparatory negotiations convened in October, it would only stimulate the emotions of Britain and the United States. It is better to wait for the outcome of the preparatory negotiations and then adopt a flexible response. However, although the preparatory conference was scheduled to be held in October, according to recent information, the United States is quite panicked by Japan's proposal to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty. Therefore, its naval plan will also deploy its main force along the Pacific coast, and it is a fact that it has moved a portion of its Atlantic Fleet's base to the Pacific coast. On the other hand, Britain, which is convening the conference, is also working to postpone the preparatory negotiations, and Britain's courage is also diminished due to the turmoil in European politics. Therefore, there is a possibility that the United States will agree to the postponement method. If the preparatory negotiations are held separately by the participating countries, it will take a considerable period of time. The Japanese Navy believes that if the preparatory negotiations are postponed until next year, then, as the Ministry of Foreign Affairs said, waiting for the outcome of the preparatory negotiations would be a missed opportunity, and there are many concerns. Regarding this point, the Navy is making every effort to severely warn about the situation in Britain and the United States in order to deal with it. (26th Japanese United News Agency Telegram)

(Tokyo) Regarding the issue of abolishing the Washington Naval Treaty, Minister of the Navy Osumi, bearing the unanimous expectations of the entire Navy, contacted various parties. First, at the two Five-Minister Conferences, he strongly argued for the necessity of abolishing the treaty. Then, Prime Minister Okada, as well as the Ministers of the Army, Foreign Affairs, Finance, and other related ministers, expressed their agreement and felt the need to quickly decide on the government's intentions. Therefore, Prime Minister Okada plans to submit the issue of treaty abolition to the Cabinet Council on the 31st of this month, or at the latest on September 4th, for endorsement. The Prime Minister will explain the proceedings of the Five-Minister Conference, which should be definitively acknowledged. However, the timing and procedures for notifying the abolition will not be predetermined. Only the general policy approved by the Cabinet Council will be announced. The details of the decision are as follows:

(1) The Japanese government, in order to break free from the constraints of existing treaties that are unfavorable to it (i.e., the Washington Treaty), has decided to abolish it. (2) The timing for notifying the abolition is set before December 31, Showa 9 (1934). The purpose of the notification is because the Navy authorities have exchanged views with the Foreign Affairs authorities, with no gaps between them, and have fully considered the objective situation. It has been decided that the Japanese Embassy in the United States will notify the U.S. State Department in writing in order to declare the unwavering belief of the Japanese government and to express the situation to those inside and outside the country. (26th Japanese Allied Press Telegram)

(Tokyo) There is a strong voice within the government requesting that Foreign Minister Hirota or Minister of the Navy Osumi be appointed as the Japanese Chief Plenipotentiary to attend next year's disarmament conference. Prime Minister Okada is also paying close attention to this. On the other hand, there are requests for former Prime Minister Saito Makoto to step forward, but this is as difficult as Prime Minister Okada stepping forward himself. Even if next year's conference breaks down, there is a need for someone with the skill and strength to declare Japan's firm attitude to the world and make it understood. Moreover, from a national standpoint, it is hoped that Minister of the Navy Osumi or Foreign Minister Hirota will be sent. (26th Electric Communications)
