Jiangxi Provincial Government 115

Refuses Local Rice Merchants to Purchase Shanghai Rice

Remaining 3,000 Bags Stored in Shanghai to be Shipped Within Days

The New Voice Agency reports that the Jiangxi Provincial Government, in order to stabilize local rice prices, has purchased 15,000 bags of Hunan and Anhui "small roller" rice from Shanghai in three batches. Local rice merchants have repeatedly requested to purchase this rice to manipulate prices, but their requests have been rejected by the authorities. At the same time, fearing that unscrupulous merchants might hoard rice, the government has temporarily stockpiled it in warehouses to suppress prices during periods of high inflation. Since rice prices in Shanghai have also risen, further purchases have been suspended. The remaining 3,000 bags from the previous shipment are scheduled to be shipped within days, and the 8,000 bags of rice scheduled for September will be shipped by the end of September.

Ministry of Railways Order 116

Rectify Joint Transportation on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway

Attract Cargo Heading North to Avoid Empty Cars Returning

Capital Ferry Crosses the River with a Load of 4,000 Tons

To improve the operations of the capital ferry, the Ministry of Railways ordered the operating hours of the ferry to be increased from twelve to twenty hours to increase the capacity for transporting goods across the river. To find ways to increase the number of vehicles crossing the river and improve the efficiency of the ferry, the Ministry specifically ordered the Nanjing-Shanghai and Tianjin-Pukou Railways to rectify joint transportation of freight cars across the river. The Nanjing-Shanghai Railway was also ordered to make efforts to attract cargo for joint transportation heading north to avoid empty cars returning. The original order is recorded as follows:

(Joint Transportation of Goods) Is developing rapidly. More than 60,000 tons of goods are accumulated at stations along the line awaiting transportation. To clear the accumulated goods, the ferry was ordered to add staff and operate extra shifts. The third step must be to increase the number of vehicles crossing the river for the plan to achieve full results. At present, there are only about 200 freight cars in Tianjin-Pukou and only about 130 in Nanjing-Shanghai that meet the conditions for joint transportation across the river. Therefore, the maximum amount of goods crossing the river daily from north to south is no more than 2,400 tons, and from south to north, it is even less, only several hundred tons. The transportation capacity is limited. The majority of other freight cars in Nanjing-Shanghai either have weak springs or low hooks. In Tianjin-Pukou, many cars lack air brakes and are not repaired, resulting in them not meeting the conditions for crossing the river. This causes the joint transportation of goods to be stockpiled at stations without being able to be transported. How can the efficiency of the ferry crossing the river be expanded if the number of vehicles crossing the river is limited? It is useless. The Ministry specifically orders the two railway bureaus to

(Undertake Rectification) The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway should replace the springs of in-service vehicles or raise the hooks. The Tianjin-Pukou Railway should repair the vehicles. By taking this measure, the number of tons of cargo will greatly increase, and the ferry's revenue will reach its highest point, which would be enough to repay the principal and interest. Furthermore, there is too little cargo transported by the Beijing-Hankou Railway from south to north, resulting in many joint transportation vehicles heading south returning empty on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway, which is uneconomical. The Beijing-Hankou Railway should make efforts to attract joint transportation of goods heading north

(To Develop Further) Also, the daily transportation limit of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway is no more than 3,200 tons, while the ferry, after improvement, can transport 4,000 tons across the river, with 800 tons of carrying capacity remaining. The Tianjin-Pukou Railway should attract several hundred tons of coal transport to supplement the load. Even if it cannot be transported to Shanghai and Hangzhou, it should at least be able to be transported across the river by ferry to Nanjing. The above items should be followed by the two railway bureaus and completed by the deadline. Plans should be made within ten days after receiving the order to implement this matter.

China and Shanghai Banks Jointly Form 117

Hunan Agricultural Product Warehouse Loan Syndicate

Eight Major Agricultural Product Warehouses Established Throughout the Province

Syndicate Responsible for Handling Mortgage Loans

Hunan is a well-known rice-producing region in China, with a large amount of rice shipped to the Yangtze River basin and Shanghai and Fujian each year. In recent years, due to frequent disasters, farmers have become increasingly impoverished, and there is a complete lack of warehousing facilities. In the event of floods or droughts, crop failures occur, and people have no way to survive. He Jian, Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government, deeply affected by this year's floods and droughts, feels that without large-scale warehousing, it is impossible to maintain the rural economy. Therefore, he drafted the Hunan Cotton Industry Experiment Field Agricultural Product Warehouse Plan and Warehouse Mortgage Loan Measures, which were discussed by Yu Jifu, Director of the Department of Reconstruction, Zhang Kailian, Director of the Department of Finance, Yuan Zhongkui, Director of the Cotton Industry Experiment Field, and Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China in Shanghai, and Chen Guangfu, General Manager of the Shanghai Bank, to negotiate investment loans. A rough agreement has now been reached to form the "Agricultural Product Warehouse Loan Bank" jointly by the Bank of China and the Shanghai Bank. Lu Zhiting and Li Jingtao have been specifically assigned to be responsible for the handling in Hunan. The details are as follows:

(Purpose of the Warehouse) Warehousing in China was established very early. During the Warring States period, Li Kui's price-balancing method existed. In the mid-Western Han dynasty, the Ever-Normal Granary system emerged. Other systems, such as community granaries and charity granaries, existed throughout the dynasties. However, to this day, they have all been abolished. The only way to remedy this is to refer to the old Ever-Normal Granary system and new cooperative regulations and to establish rural warehouses in conjunction with news agencies so that farmers can obtain funds for emergency needs without having to sell their products at low prices. Moreover, warehouses can purchase food at fair prices to regulate supply and demand. In the event of unexpected national events, they can also provide emergency relief. The provincial government and the financial community jointly plan to build warehouses throughout the province and set up factories in areas with convenient transportation for processing to be sold directly to farmers by cooperatives, eliminating the exploitation of merchants.

(Regional Establishment) The province now plans to divide the province's abundant agricultural areas into eight regions, each with a regional warehouse in the transportation center of each region, with a syndicate-designated office inside. Sub-warehouses will be established in each city and town in the region, and branch warehouses will be established in small rural towns as needed. The plan is as follows: (1) Jinshi District, under the jurisdiction of Lixian, Anxiang, and Linli; (2) Changde District, under the jurisdiction of Changde, Taoyuan, and Hanshou; (3) Yiyang District, under the jurisdiction of Yiyang and Yuanjiang; (4) Nanhua District, under the jurisdiction of Nanxian and Huarong; (5) Yueyang District, under the jurisdiction of Yueyang, Linxiang, and Pingjiang; (6) Jinggang District, under the jurisdiction of Changsha, Ningxiang, Xiangyin, and Liuyang; (7) Zhuzhou District, under the jurisdiction of Xiangtan, Liling, Youxian, Hengshan, and Xiangxiang; (8) Hengyang District, under the jurisdiction of Hengyang, Laiyang, Qiyang, Changning, and Anren. As for the construction costs, regional and sub-warehouses will be provided by the provincial treasury, while branch warehouses will be raised by the local area. Warehouse management and maintenance costs will be provided by warehouse rental income.

(Syndicate Loans) The loan method has been agreed upon by the Hunan Provincial Government and the syndicate and has been submitted to the Provincial Government meeting for approval. The reporter from the Shenshi News Agency has learned that the main provisions of its contents are as follows: (1) The agricultural products pledged in the warehouse are temporarily limited to five types: rice, cotton seeds, broad beans, soybeans, and wheat. (2) Warehouse loans will first be offered to cooperative farmers in the Hunan Agricultural Experiment Field and then gradually extended to other farmers. (3) The agricultural products pledged in the warehouse are limited to the products produced by each farmer, ranging from one dan to one hundred dan, which will be accepted. Those who sell and hoard will not be accepted. (4) The loan interest rate should be low. The tentative rate is one percent per month, with one mill extracted from it as the warehouse reserve fund, and the rest goes to the investing syndicate. (5) The pledged agricultural products must be paid for insurance premiums, which cannot exceed one mill. Warehouse management and maintenance fees must also be paid, with five mills per dan of rice, two and a half cents per dan of beans and wheat, and five cents per dan of cotton seeds per month. (6) Farmers who obtain benefits from the warehouse (calculated based on the market price on the date of entry into the warehouse and the price of the sale of the redeemable food, not limited to this), should deposit one-third of it into the syndicate for savings for famine, which cannot be withdrawn unless there is a disaster or special event.

(Jinshi First) The establishment of the warehouse will begin with Jinshi. All types of warehouses in the region are expected to be completed within three years, starting from 1934. A regional warehouse with a capacity of approximately 50,000 dan has now been established in Jinshi, a branch warehouse with a capacity of approximately 20,000 dan in Licheng, Xinzhou, Anxiang, and Xinan, and a branch warehouse with a capacity of approximately 5,000 dan in each village. In the summer of this year, the syndicate has already made production loans of 22,584 yuan in the Jinshi area. This is only a trial, and it will gradually expand to the countryside and other regions. Yuan Zhongda, Director of the Provincial Agricultural Experiment Field, Lu Zhiting, Manager of the Bank of China in Changsha, and Li Jingtao, Manager of the Shanghai Bank in Changsha, will be responsible for presiding over everything.

Severe Drought in Jing County, Anhui 118

Fellow Villagers in Shanghai Are Telegraphically Requested for Relief

Since the fourth month of the lunar calendar, a severe drought has ravaged Jing County in southern Anhui Province. Rainfall has been scarce, and all the fields in the countryside are parched. Farmers are in despair over the crop failure, and some entire families have committed suicide, which is truly tragic. The public organizations in the county, recognizing the severity of the disaster, have sent telegrams to the Central Relief Committee and the Anhui Provincial authorities, requesting relief, and have also sent telegrams to fellow villagers in Shanghai, appealing for help. The original telegram is recorded as follows:

To Mr. Zhu Rushan, Mr. Wei Shoujing, forwarded to Mr. Hu Pu, Mr. Zhu Dou, Mr. Zhu Jing, and all fellow villagers of Shanghai, Jingjian:

We have recently sent telegrams to Commander-in-Chief Jiang in Nanchang, Xu, Chairman of the Central Relief Committee, Liu, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, Miao, Special Commissioner of the Anhui Provincial Party Department, Mao, Director of the Anhui Department of Finance, Ma, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, the Anhui Relief Committee, Zhou, Administrative Inspector of Xuancheng, the Shanghai Sino-Foreign Relief Association, the Shanghai Jisheng Society, the Shanghai Red Cross Society, and the Shanghai Red Wanzihui, stating: Jing County is located in the mountains, and the fields are mostly barren. Even in good years, they are insufficient. However, since April 8th of this year's lunar calendar, a severe drought has ravaged the area. Rainfall has been scarce, and the fields are all parched. The crops have withered, and streams have dried up. Only a line of water remains in the large river, and drinking water is difficult in various places. Although we have sincerely prayed to Sanglin and made every effort to irrigate, hoping to remedy the situation, the wind god has been evil, and the sun crow has been unkind, and we have not been able to succeed. After investigation, the disaster area throughout the county has exceeded eight-tenths, and the number of disaster victims has reached more than 100,000, which is an unprecedented disaster and an unprecedented catastrophe. Moreover, since 1928, we have repeatedly suffered from banditry, coupled with years of famine. Our vitality has not recovered, and there is a lack of storage. In this strange famine, cries fill the fields, and the hungry fill the roads. Thousands of starving people are looking for food, and there is no way to provide relief. The most tragic thing is that the Hu family in Beixiang had seven family members who committed suicide by taking poison due to lack of food, and the entire family died. The Zhang Bao family in Nanxiang also hanged themselves due to unbearable hunger. Other similar deaths occur from time to time. In this dangerous situation, if we do not urgently request relief, not only will the lives of more than 100,000 disaster victims not be guaranteed, but also the security of the entire county will be difficult to maintain. We urge your council (seat) to show compassion and immediately provide emergency relief to save the disaster victims who are dying and to maintain the precarious situation. The telegram cannot express our urgency to await your orders.

We hope that you, gentlemen, will care about your hometown and be concerned about the hungry and drowning. Please unanimously act separately to appeal and solicit donations to save the disaster victims. We look forward to it and pray earnestly.

Zhu Chengxiang, Party Department of Jing County; Zuo Ziju, Finance Committee; Cao Ziyu, Chamber of Commerce; Pan Junfu, Education Association; Wang Weichun, Farmers' Association; Zhao Yiquan and Zuo Shaowen, Representatives of the First District; Zhu Xiagu and Hu Xiqiu, Representatives of the Second District; Wang Songwen and Chen Like, Representatives of the Third District; Bao Shixuan and Wang Aiting, Representatives of the Fourth District; Dong Boren and Ma Zhongchang, Representatives of the Fifth District; Wei Mengyan and Shen Yunxian, Representatives of the Sixth District; Li Baoshan, Two Hunan Fellow Villagers Association; Zhu Yishao, Anqing Fellow Villagers Association; Zhang Xuanhong, Jindou Fellow Villagers Association; Cheng Xiting, Huizhou Fellow Villagers Association, and others kowtow. Ma Yin.

Problem of Rice Industry Collecting Dockage Fees 119

The rice industry in Xuejiabang, Nanshi, built docks specifically for rice. Because rice ships from various ports arrive in Shanghai and the county docks are used for berthing and unloading, the rice firms paid for the construction of the docks. It was agreed that one cent per stone would be collected for rice shipped from inland to Shanghai as a dockage fee. The collection of the fee would be stopped once the amount paid by each firm was recovered. The collection of the fee began in 1929 and has lasted for six years. However, the rice firms in the interior reported that the amount of dockage fees paid had already reached the target amount, so they wrote to inquire. The Rice Merchants Association inquired, and if the amount was reached, they were asked to negotiate with the Bean and Rice Firm. However, the fee is still being collected this year. Therefore, in June, rice firms from various ports in the interior sent representatives to Shanghai specifically to hold a joint meeting to discuss countermeasures. They decided to ask the Rice Merchants Association to send a letter to the Bean and Rice Firm, requesting that a detailed account of the one cent dockage fee paid be announced before the end of June. If there was no satisfactory response, they would unanimously stop paying the fee starting in July. It has now been two months, and there has been no definite response. Therefore, in recent days, rice firms from various ports in the interior have sent representatives to Shanghai or written letters to the Rice Merchants Association to inquire and negotiate. Yesterday, the representatives who arrived in Shanghai held a special meeting with the rice ships that sell rice themselves to discuss countermeasures.

Second Special District 120

Court to Improve Prison

Addition of Sanitary Equipment and Other Items

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Second Special District Court and the Third Branch of the High Court previously considered the existing detention center to be extremely small and planned to build a new prison, with the old prison to be used as a detention center. Wang Simao, President of the Second Special District Court, told the Central News Agency reporter that the construction of a new prison is not only lacking funds but also that there would be no source of ongoing expenses after the new prison was built. Therefore, this proposal has been shelved. The court is currently improving the old prison, such as establishing workshops, which have all been implemented. The average number of inmates in the prison is approximately 1,000, so there is no overcrowding. As for the detention center, it is considered to be simple and small. Sanitary equipment and other items are being added to improve it as much as possible in the unavoidable situation. On the other hand, the court is negotiating with the police to shorten the period for waiving appeals as much as possible to reduce the number of detainees and to provide the people with due protection.

Two Organizations on Avenue Edward VII 121

Send Letters Requesting Suppression of Street Prostitutes

The 14th Branch of the United Association of Citizens in the First Special District and the Avenue Edward VII Business Association yesterday sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers Association, which forwarded it to the Public Works Department, requesting the suppression of street prostitutes ("wild chickens") who forcibly solicit customers. The letter states:

To whom it may concern:

According to shopkeepers and citizens in the Zhengjia Muqiao, Dongxinqiao, and Xizang Road areas of Avenue Edward VII, when the lights come on at night, pimps from brothels drive out prostitutes, who are covered in powder and stink. They are a ghastly sight. It is just like a prostitution market. They line up against each other, and the door is blocked. When passers-by pass by, they are forcibly solicited, regardless of their intentions. If they encounter single villagers or merchants, they will drag them en masse and even rob them of their belongings, which is like robbery. As a result, passers-by are afraid to pass by and regard it as a dangerous path, which hinders the business of shops and causes huge losses. Although these prostitutes have licenses, the Public Works Department stipulates that they are only allowed to receive customers at the entrance of the brothel and are not allowed to forcibly solicit customers arbitrarily. Although the Public Works Department occasionally sends people to arrest them, these prostitutes are vigilant and densely distributed. They avoid capture by calling out to each other, making it impossible for the police to exercise their authority. We should suppress them to protect customers.

After the association sent staff to investigate, the matter was submitted for discussion at the meeting. Everyone agreed that the rampant behavior of these prostitutes is extremely illegal, not only hindering business but also hindering the development of municipal administration. If they are not strictly suppressed, everyone will suffer. At a minimum, we should ask the Public Works Department to effectively suppress them in accordance with the regulations. Otherwise, we demand that the authorities stop issuing business licenses to prostitutes in the area and order them to move to quiet places to get rid of the filth.

Correspondingly, we are sending this letter to your association based on the case, requesting that you promptly forward it to the Public Works Department and find a way to effectively suppress them.

New Development of Ningbo Industrial Bank 124

Promoting Domestic Production and Supporting Foreign Trade

The Ningbo Industrial Bank, located at No. 500 Henan Road in Shanghai, has been established since its inception. The bank is mainly engaged in industry, commerce, fisheries, various mortgage loans, and national goods circulation mortgage loans. With the development of its business, branches were added in Ningbo and Shenjiamen, specializing in financial assistance to the fishing industry, such as fisherman loans, fishery remittances, and other businesses, which have greatly promoted the development of the fishing industry and achieved remarkable results. The local fishermen have benefited from it. Loans are released during the fishing season and repaid on time, benefiting both the bank and the fishermen. The Shanghai head office specializes in factory goods mortgage loans and national goods circulation mortgage loans, free remittance services, and economic small loans, which promote the development of industry and the promotion of national goods. On the one hand, it connects with the same industry and provides financial assistance to foreign trade, so that the excellent products of various provinces in China can participate in the Chicago Exposition, which has been praised by people from various countries, and has a great effect on promoting culture and foreign trade. This year, a branch was added in Suzhou, and Mr. Wu Songlu, a senior banker, was hired to preside over everything. The business has also been developing well. Recently, two warehouses have been established in Kunshan to first handle mortgage loans for farmers. After achieving results, other businesses will be expanded. The bank will also cooperate with the same industry and gentry and merchants in the area. It is reported that the bank's original building is not enough for office use, so it has selected the Water Gate Steel Bone Building at No. 261 Nanjing Road, the intersection of Shanxi Road, as its new address. The interior is currently being renovated, and it will be moved on the 19th of next month.

Arriving Today

The British Hamilton Circus has been world-renowned for more than 40 years. This time, it has returned to Shanghai with new and unique stunts that are ten times more exciting than its last performance in Shanghai. Prices range from 50 cents for side boxes to 20 yuan for large boxes (accommodating six people). There are six levels in total. Children under 12 years old are sold half-price for day performances.

Fumin Road 127

A Robbery at a Cigarette and Paper Shop - One Thief Captured

At approximately 7 PM yesterday, a cigarette and paper shop named Yi Da He, located at number 157 Fumin Road within the jurisdiction of the Second Precinct, Second Substation of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau, was suddenly invaded by two robbers dressed in black shirts and trousers. Under the pretense of being customers, one of the robbers brandished a handgun, warning them not to make a sound. They then robbed the shop of approximately over a hundred yuan in cash and silver coins, as well as a gold ring worn by the shop owner’s wife. After acquiring their loot, they fled in separate directions. Zhang Xin’gen (18 years old), a local apprentice at the shop, was quite quick-witted. Seeing the robbers leave, he secretly followed behind, giving chase. However, when one of the robbers reached Penglai Road, he realized he was being followed. He then fired two shots as a warning, while Zhang Xin’gen simultaneously shouted for help to catch the thief. Immediately, police whistles sounded. The robber then fled into Liu Xing Lane within the First Precinct, reaching Caojia Bridge. At this time, police officer Song Yuting from Post 30 had already pursued him closely. As a result, he was finally intercepted by police officer Zhang Zukun from Post 31. At the time, Shen Zhenhua, the chief of the First Precinct, was leading many senior officers on patrol nearby. Hearing the commotion, they immediately rushed to the scene, taking both the robber and the apprentice Zhang Xin’gen to the station. At the same time, the police also found a six-inch Browning pistol (number 3083) discarded by the robber inside a short wall in Liu Xing Lane, containing four bullets. Initially, Zhang Xin’gen provided a clear account of the robbery situation. Upon interrogation, the robber confessed that his name was Zhang Changsheng, 35 years old, from Hefei, Anhui. He readily admitted to being involved with a gang. After the interrogation, Chief Liu immediately telegraphed the Inspectorate and promptly prepared a document to be submitted to the Judicial Section for questioning.

Shanghai-Nantong-Jingjiang-Taixing Telephone Service 133

Officially Opens Tomorrow

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and the Jiangsu Provincial Long-Distance Telephone Administration have been preparing since this spring to facilitate telephone communication between Nantong, Jingjiang, Taixing, and Shanghai. Yesterday, the Telephone Bureau received a telegram from the Administration stating that the construction of the telephone lines in all three locations has been completed. Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Animals 135

Prohibiting the Killing of Animals

Requesting Orders from the Two Concession Municipal Councils

Following the Precedent of the Former Mixed Court

The Chinese Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Animals believes that Western countries have long established special laws and incorporated them into their legal systems to protect animals, and these laws have been quite effective since their implementation. In recent times, leaders from Britain, America, Italy, Germany, France, and Japan have been the most vigorous advocates, and their efforts have been widely reported and admired worldwide. As for our Chinese gentry, due to their early civilization, they all possess a benevolent and compassionate heart. Therefore, they have also established societies to promote animal protection movements, hoping to achieve the ideal of treating animals as fellow beings. However, in Shanghai, where Chinese and foreigners live together, people are of varying qualities, and conscience is easily lost. There are often gluttonous individuals who indulge their appetites and treat the abuse or killing of animals as commonplace. For example, pigeons are suffocated with ropes around their mouths, mountain chickens have their tongues cut and bleed to death, various snails are subjected to the death of having their tails cut off alive, chickens and ducks are tied up and hung upside down before slaughter, live frogs are skinned and sold, and so on. These sights are common in vegetable markets and thoroughfares. The former Mixed Court had strictly prohibited such behavior, and offenders were punished with fines or imprisonment, as a slight deterrent. This was because innocent animals were unfortunate enough to be cooked and eaten, but it was even worse to subject them to inhumane treatment at the time of their death, causing them to struggle and suffer. Anyone with a human heart would abhor this. The intention was to persuade through prohibition, and the law was both beautiful and good. However, since the reorganization of the Mixed Court into the Special District Court, this strict prohibition has been relaxed, causing unscrupulous residents to become complacent over time and gradually return to their old ways. Therefore, the Society specifically sent a letter to the Municipal Councils of the two concessions yesterday, ordering all police stations to continue to follow the strict prohibition measures of the former Mixed Court, and to supervise Chinese and foreign detectives to conduct thorough investigations and issue notices prohibiting the abuse and killing of animals, to answer to Heaven and maintain the laws of the people. If there are any who outwardly comply but inwardly defy, stubbornly clinging to their evil ways, they should be severely punished to preserve animal life and curb the cruel customs, so that the killing can be stopped and world peace can be achieved.

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday After Being Towed

Cargo Transferred - Wu Yang Steamer Sails to Hong Kong and Guangdong

To Enter Dock for Repairs After Cargo is Offloaded

The Yushun steamer of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company suffered engine damage in the waters off Fuzhou and was unable to navigate. The head office telegraphed the Wuyang steamer to go to the rescue.

Red Pill King 137

Zhou Shengfa Released to the District Court

Prosecutor Waited for Trial That Night

Zhou Shengfa, the Red Pill King from Yuyao, raised a large amount of capital this spring and privately set up a large-scale organization at No. 1382 Longhua Road in Nanshi to manufacture Feima brand red pills, which were exclusively sold in Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, Luoyang, and other ports. Branch offices were established in each of these locations for secret sales, with astonishing quantities. Although the time was short, the profits were already substantial. On February 4th, the Municipal Public Security Bureau seized 2.4 million red pills worth over 200,000 yuan at the North Railway Station, and arrested key criminals Zhao Zuting and Wang Weicheng (also known as Xiao Wang), as well as three police officers who were found to be sheltering and transporting the goods. They were handed over to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for investigation and were all executed by firing squad. However, Wang Weicheng's confession revealed that the mastermind Zhou Shengfa had escaped. Despite extensive searches, he had not been apprehended until recently, when Detective Ling Tianpeng of the Public Security Bureau received a tip from an informant that Zhou was hiding at No. 20, Lane 707, Yuanyuan Lane, Gordon Road in the Public Concession. Together with Chinese and foreign detectives, they went to the address and arrested Zhou, handing him over to the First Special District Court. The day before yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi opened a court session for preliminary interrogation. The Public Security Bureau ordered Detective Ling Tianpeng to present a document requesting the transfer of Zhou Shengfa for questioning, but Zhou stubbornly refused to confess. As a result, the judge ruled that the suspect Zhou Shengfa be transferred to the District Court Procuratorate for investigation. At 5:30 PM, the First Special District Court first notified the Nanshi District Court Procuratorate by telephone, stating that the 26th of the following day (i.e., yesterday) was a Sunday, and the 27th was also Confucius's birthday, so offices would be closed. Therefore, they were allowed to transfer the suspect Zhou that night. Chief Prosecutor Lou Ying of the District Court then instructed the prosecutor on duty, Lei Binzhang, to postpone leaving and wait until 8:35 PM, when the First Special District Court ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to escort the suspect Zhou Shengfa to the District Court, where Prosecutor Lei opened a court session for investigation and ordered him to be properly detained. By the time Zhou was taken into custody at the detention center, it was already 9:00 PM.

Pu Wenting Case 140

Kidnappers Sent Back for Retrial

Trial Concluded, Sentence Scheduled

Pu Wenting, the manager of Fuxin Flour Mill from Wuxi, and Qian Zhaofu, the owner of a local timber firm in Nanshi, were kidnapped in the French Concession four years ago and held for a large ransom. After the case broke, the French police apprehended the kidnappers, Zheng Shifan and Zhang Afu, both locals, and handed them over to the Second Special District Court. In the first instance, Zheng was sentenced to life imprisonment and Zhang to 20 years. Zheng and the others were dissatisfied and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. As a result, Zheng's sentence was reduced to 12 years of imprisonment, and Zhang's sentence was changed to life imprisonment. Because the two convicts were still unwilling to accept the verdict, they filed a third appeal with the Supreme Court. After reviewing the entire case file, the Supreme Court found that there was still a question about Zheng Shifan borrowing a telephone at a certain exchange to contact the victims. Therefore, it ruled to overturn the original verdict and send the case back to the Third Branch of the High Court for retrial, as reported in previous news. The Third Branch of the High Court has ordered the police station to conduct a new investigation and summon witnesses to the case. After completing the interrogation, presiding Judge Guo Dexin, along with associate judges Sun and Fan, and Prosecutor Zhang, opened a joint court session for trial on the morning of the day before yesterday. Attorney Yao Zhaodi represented the Police Department and made detailed statements against the appellants' points of appeal. Attorneys Ma Shouhua and others defended the appellants. The court then announced the conclusion of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 31st. The appellants were returned to the detention center to await the verdict.

Huamei Offers Scholarships Again 141

Election of Historical Greats

Commemorating the Sales Success of Guanghua Brand Cigarettes

Last year, the China Huamei Tobacco Company's "Buy a Stick" scholarship program received high praise from society. Now, with the sales success of its Guanghua brand of Chinese standard cigarettes, the company's general manager Jing Yimeng, co-managers Wang Yongchang, Yu Zhong'e, and others have decided to save on advertising and promotional expenses to offer the Chinese Historical Greats Election Scholarship again. This move, in addition to benefiting young people, allows everyone to examine the ancient people and understand what made them able to glorify China, promote their spirit, strengthen their will, and be pioneers for the country and serve society. The meaning is great and worth introducing. The methods have been drafted and will be announced soon. Here is their declaration:

The long history of our nation, the richness and brilliance of our cultural achievements, the fact that we are an ancient country in East Asia, and more advanced than Europe and America, are all derived from the crystallization of the thoughts and deeds of great men of all generations. The reason why great men could be produced in all generations cannot but be attributed to education. However, in today's society, with the decline of the social economy and the high cost of living, even a family of eight can hardly make ends meet, let alone afford education. Young people lose the opportunity to study, and they regret it when they get old. This is a hidden worry of society and a regret for young people. Our company has always held the great ambition that everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the world, believing that the key to a wealthy country and a strong people is not at the top but at the bottom, not to be blamed on the government but to be the responsibility of the people. It is not difficult to enrich the country, revitalizing domestic goods is enough. It is not difficult to strengthen the people, promoting education is enough. The government and the people are responsible for revitalizing domestic goods and promoting education. Over the years, we have been thinking about this day and night. Therefore, to the best of our ability, at the time of the prosperous sales of our company's Guanghua brand Chinese standard cigarettes, we will save advertising and promotional expenses and transfer them to scholarships for the election of historically great men. Selling domestic goods in order to enrich the country, promoting education in order to strengthen the people. We hope that all parents who love to smoke domestic Guanghua brand cigarettes will collect the small blue Guanghua stamped stickers or the empty Guanghua brand ten-pack boxes and give them to their children to use for the election of historically great men. In the study, after dinner, parents enjoy the clean and happy experience of domestic cigarettes, and children enjoy the right to vote and receive educational scholarships. Enriching the country and strengthening the people can be achieved in one fell swoop. Our company has already conducted a trial run of awarding scholarships once before, and it has been well-received by society. However, we still feel that it is not enough, so we will continue to make persistent efforts to continue to hold the event. Our sincere intention is to not only benefit young people but also enable everyone to think deeply, examine how the ancients were able to achieve a renaissance through one success and one trip, how they were able to endure hardship and defeat their enemies, and how they were able to plant trees for ten years and cultivate people for a hundred years, to cultivate outstanding talents who can directly attack the Yellow Dragon and recover lost land. All of these are historical materials that today's young students must study. The ancients have passed away, but the righteous spirit of heaven and earth and the brilliance of history will always be a model for future generations. We hope that we can contribute to the enrichment of the country and the strengthening of the people while promoting domestic goods.

Cigarette and Exchange Industry Association 143

Requests Exemption from Re-Levying of Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax

Small Businesses Unable to Bear the Burden

Submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for Further Request

The tobacco and alcohol industries in this city, regarding the issue of re-levying licenses, due to uneven treatment in tax assessment and investigation, the Shanghai South Office of the Cigarette and Exchange Industry Association yesterday received a joint letter signed by over a hundred businesses, including Baoxin at No. 51 Houjia Road in the city, Chengchang at No. 14 Wei Wu Branch Road, No. 355 Jumen Road, etc., stating, "We received a notice from your association to register with the Finance Bureau as scheduled and apply for tax payment and licensing. However, after a few days, the investigators from the Tax Assessment Office said that each license would require an additional two yuan. We went to the office, but it was a weekday and they were closed. We went to collect them the next day, but they wanted to add 2.4 yuan. We are small husband-and-wife shops, making a living with meager capital, and unable to bear the burden. When the Ministry of Finance collected taxes, it was still able to sympathize, collecting only two yuan per quarter. The central government, in view of the bankruptcy of rural areas and the depression of all industries, abolished harsh and miscellaneous taxes, with the aim of reducing the burden on citizens. Merchants were overjoyed and grateful. However, the cigarettes we sell have already paid the consolidated tax and regular tax, and the license should be tax-exempt. Now, the Finance Bureau not only does not exempt us, but also increases the tax. Our small businesses cannot bear the heavy burden. We have no choice but to jointly write to your association and send the attached receipts, requesting that you forward them to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, imploring the Finance Bureau to consider the difficulties of the merchants and approve the issuance of new licenses to show sympathy and maintain our businesses." It is reported that the association has already compiled a list based on this and submitted it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce as the second batch of requests.

Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Demands Equal Tax Levies 144

Handle According to Regulations, Divide into Grades

In Order to Reduce the Suffering of Small Businesses

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, the uneven distribution of tobacco and alcohol taxes has aroused opposition from the industry. They have requested the industry association to forward their request to the Municipal Finance Bureau for correction. As of yesterday, the issue had not yet been resolved. Yesterday, we inquired at the South District Office of the Industry Association. According to the person in charge, "Our association is a group of industry members, seeking to facilitate the business of the entire industry. We have repeatedly received reports from members that the grades of tax levies are uneven, which is not conducive to stable business operations. We request that the Municipal Government authorities correct this and reduce the suffering of small businesses. According to our investigation, in the 16th year of the Republic, taxes were levied twice a year, at two yuan per term. In the 17th year, it was changed to four seasons per year, but still two yuan per quarter, which effectively added four yuan per year. In recent years, tax levies have often not been handled according to regulations. Large stores pay less, while family industries or small shops pay more, creating a distorted situation. Therefore, reports have been submitted to our association. We have previously petitioned the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to request fair measures to ensure balance so that the members of our industry can gradually become stable."

Madwoman Harasses American Consulate 146

Previously Caused Trouble at Hall and Holtz

Injured a Female Shop Assistant with an Umbrella

Also Claimed to be the Egyptian Goddess

Regarding the incident reported yesterday of a madwoman harassing the American Consul General's Office, according to the North China Daily News, the madwoman's name is Pike, 19 years old, residing at No. 62 Donghuai De Road. Before harassing the American Consul General's Office, she went to Hall and Holtz on Nanjing Road and struck female shop assistants Huimeier and Velilla with an umbrella. When the two women fled to another room, Ms. Pike also went into the road and disappeared. The two female shop assistants then went to the Central Police Station to report the incident, stating that they recognized the assailant as Ms. Pike. Ms. Huimeier suffered minor injuries to her hand, and Ms. Velilla suffered minor abrasions to her lips. When asked about the reason for the attack, they replied that it was probably because one of them shared a young boyfriend with Ms. Pike, and it was caused by jealousy. While the two women were still at the police station, the fire brigade's ambulance arrived with Ms. Pike. It was then learned that Ms. Pike had gone to the American Consul General's Office to make a scene after leaving Hall and Holtz. Ms. Pike claimed to be an American citizen, but the American authorities did not recognize her. Later, her mother was summoned and ordered to take her back and restrain her, and she was given a warning. According to the police investigation, the woman's father was an American naval officer, and her mother was Japanese. The daughter was born after the father went to the United States. Therefore, neither the American nor the Japanese consulate recognized the woman or her mother. When the woman harassed the American Consul General's Office, she claimed to be the Egyptian goddess and a close friend of the British Prince.

Water Outage in Huakangli 149

Rent Arrears Should Be Handled According to Law

Water Supply Should Not Be Cut Off

In Huakangli, Huakang Road, Zhabei, the landlord cut off the water supply the day before yesterday (Sunday, the 5th) due to some reason. More than ten sub-tenants, including Ji Ruyou, jointly submitted a petition to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, requesting relief. This matter was reported in the newspapers. It is now known that after the Fourth District Chief Gong reviewed the report, he repeatedly ordered the landlord, Tan Fuji, to appear, but he never did. Yesterday afternoon, Tan Li, the sister-in-law of Tan Fuji, was summoned. According to her, the tenants in the alley were using too much water, so she had previously agreed with the tenants to switch to well water. However, the cost of digging the well was to be shared by the tenants, but now the tenants are unwilling to pay and owe a lot of rent, so the water was cut off. Ji Ruyou and others stated, "We do not owe rent, and Tan Fuji not only cut off the water supply but also ordered us to move out. We request relief." After questioning, the officials believed that if the tenants owed too much rent, they could apply to the court for mediation. If mediation failed, they could formally file a lawsuit. As for the water supply, it should not be cut off and should be opened immediately to resolve the matter.

Railway Bureau Today 150

Opens Special Train for Haining Tidal Bore Viewing

After Arriving in Chang'an, Transfer to Automobile to Go to Haining

Every autumn, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus specially open trains for the Haining tidal bore. This year, they are starting early, on August 27th, 28th, September 11th, 12th, 26th, and 27th, a total of six days. The train departs from Shanghai North Station at 7:55 AM and arrives in Chang'an at 11:31 AM, where passengers transfer to automobiles to Haining. The round-trip ticket price from Shanghai North Station to Haining is 12.15 yuan for first class, 8.15 yuan for second class, and 5.50 yuan for third class. The above prices include round-trip tickets for the train and automobile, as well as admission to the tidal bore viewing park. It is also stipulated that the number of automobile tickets is limited to 150 for August 27th and 28th, and 200 for September 11th, 12th, 26th, and 27th. In previous years, people took small steam-powered boats from Xieqiao to Haining. This year, they will travel by automobile from Chang'an.

Sunken Ship Discovered in Eastern Coastal Waters 151

Hydrographic Office Notifies the Maritime Community

A sunken ship has been discovered in the western entrance of the Sanpan-Dongtou Strait on the east coast. One mast and the smokestack are exposed above the water. The Hydrographic Office has issued a notice to the maritime community, reminding them to pay attention, as the location of the sunken ship is on a main shipping route. The sunken ship is located 26 degrees north of Niu Shi Reef, at a distance of two chains (every ten chains equals one nautical mile), which is approximately 121 degrees and 5 minutes east longitude and 27 degrees and 49 minutes north latitude.

Publication of "Qingliang Mountain Chronicle": Qingliang Mountain, that is, West Wutai Mountain, is the place where the Bodhisattva Manjusri manifested himself and is one of the four famous mountains in China. The scenery is deep and secluded, and there are often many spiritual wonders. Ancient temples and monasteries fill the rocks and caves. In the early Tang Dynasty, Master Langu created the "Qingliang Biography Collection." In the Song Dynasty, the monk Yanyi made a "Broad Biography," and Wu Jushi made a "Continuation Biography." During the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty, the monk Zhenhai based on the old books to write the "Qingliang Mountain Chronicle," which is the most comprehensive. Recently, Master Yinguang visited the old chronicles by all means and re-edited and revised them with Jushi Xu Zhijing. The content is detailed and perfect. The preface of the book has a frontispiece of Master Yinguang, and the calligraphic inscription on the eyebrow of the book is written by Mr. Ye Gongchuo, a contemporary celebrity. The copperplate-printed statue of Manjusri is particularly valuable. This book is rare in the market. Buddhist monks and laity should have one copy, and those who are interested in famous places, study local chronicles, and collect books must have one. The entire book is divided into two volumes and is priced at a special low price of only one yuan and two jiao. There are not many books left, so please buy them quickly. Published by the Buddhist Bookstore on Jiaozhou Road.

Reading Q&A

On Practice and Pragmatism 165

— Reply to Mr. Tan Mengruo —

After reading our "Explanation of Practice," Mr. Tan wrote to ask: What is pragmatism? Pragmatism and practice are easily confused, hence Mr. Tan's confusion.

Pragmatism, as the name suggests, places great importance on practical effect. Anything useful is a good thing. Any useful speech is the truth. If we take it a step further, it becomes utilitarianism, where everything is measured by benefit and effectiveness, regardless of anything else. We cannot say that this doctrine is completely unreasonable. Since people must live, they cannot ignore the benefits of life. If my life compels me to use an abacus every day, and I refuse to do so, wouldn't I starve to death? If I starve to death, how can I care about anything else?

However, we must pay attention to the fact that pragmatism places too much importance, too much emphasis on the effects of application, measuring everything by practicality, and obliterating all theories and truths. There are many people in the world who specialize in practicality. They say that doing things must be down-to-earth, and they consider all theories to be empty talk. "Empty talk is of no use in practice." This is true, but to negate even all reasonable and scientific theories because of opposition to empty talk is a big mistake. Because, if we are aiming to be sloppy, muddling through, then of course we don’t need any theory. If we want to broaden our horizons, to make our lives more advanced, to make our actions go in a more correct direction, then we cannot do without the guidance of theory.

Taking reading as an example, if we look at it entirely from a practical point of view, then novels of the Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School can provide us with entertainment, and of course they have practical value. Jokes can make us smile after hard work, which is also very practical. These things can have a temporary paralyzing effect on our spirits, making us forget the pain of life, isn’t that also good? However, the practical effect of these things is only to be able to deceive our eyes, making us unable to see the painful reality around us, making our lives without purpose, making us decadent. If we want to understand the society around us, to determine a correct direction for our efforts, these things are still of no use to us. In this case, we won't get any results except by studying scientific theories.

Therefore, pragmatism, which completely denies theory, has a "practical" effect that is limited to dealing with the present and cannot produce further effects. As long as we broaden our horizons a little, we will know that this narrow practical concept is still useless in the end!

If we are not just muddling through life, resigned to fate, if we are to struggle and move forward, then we must first clearly understand our surroundings, and then we can find the right path. Without the help of theory, it is impossible to understand this complex society clearly. Theory can help us understand, and that is the use of theory. Therefore, the theory despised by pragmatists is actually more practical than pragmatism itself.

Therefore, narrow pragmatism is undesirable. But now we must pay attention to another point, that is, although we oppose narrow pragmatism, we cannot regard theory as omnipotent. We must also remember the saying "Empty talk of theory is of no use in practice." Theory in books alone is of no use. The theory in books is only enough for reference, as an aid to our lives and actions. We must also take the things in books to practical life for verification. Sometimes, we can find richer things in life than in books. And we must also remember that all the theories in books originally come from the practical lives and practical research of many people. Practical life is the real source of living theory.

On the one hand, we must use theory to guide life, and on the other hand, we must use life to correct theory, and discover new theories in life. This is practice. Practice is the unity of "pragmatism" and "theory." Pragmatism is not practice, and empty theory is not practice.

Free Talk

On Being Humane 168

— Yi

There are all kinds of people in the world: white people, black people, and yellow people. In ancient times, the yellow race was self-respecting, believing that apart from themselves, all other races were beasts. The translators of the "Office in Charge of Affairs of All Nations" did not regard the other races as human beings. The honorifics "Feilanxi" and "Yingjieli" are clear evidence of this.

Now we know that there are other people in the world besides ourselves, but within the same society, there are also distinctions between rich people, poor people, important people, and great people. Even among human beings, there are distinctions between men and women.

This is like talking to a child, and there should be no suspicion of being too difficult or obscure. But there is a common abusive word that people use, which is "inhumane." What kind of humanity should this refer to?

Bathing frequently and changing into clean clothes should be humane, but if the person is poor, then it is eccentric and extravagant; if the person is rich, then it is humane. In the United States, working eight hours a day is normal. In China (if it is a young master or old master), stipulating a certain number of working hours per day is inhumane. In general, this phrase encompasses all things that are Europeanized, modernized, and do not conform to ordinary people. And this vague standard is determined by the speaker's delusions.

Ji Shuye once liked blacksmithing, which seemed inhumane, but the inhumane aspect of the members of the imperial family was their elegance. If they committed evil deeds, ordinary people would not dare to oppose them. If it were a commoner, he might have been beaten long ago. In the Six Dynasties, some people even liked to give people the cold shoulder, which can be considered extremely eccentric, but no one dared to oppose him. It can be seen that even if public opinion recognizes someone as a bad egg, or as being inhumane, there are still concerns or reticence due to their status and class.

Conversely, all cunning and treacherous people are sure to be extremely humane. It is said that treacherous officials throughout history were mostly kind and amiable. Wang Mang was actually humble and respectful to scholars. Only fools who want to reform society are willing to bear the slanders of the times and endure hardships. People like Wang Jinggong have long been subjected to this four-character curse.

Those who are determined to do things should really ignore the murky criticisms. Those who cater to human emotions too much, unless they have ulterior motives, are simply fools, for sure.

Glimpses of a Malay Village (Part 2) 169

— Feier

Every evening, piles of dry firewood and dead leaves would gather at the corner of the "Attap" house, and a fire would be lit, filling the house with smoke that made it hard to breathe. While the mosquitoes were being smoked away, the stench of urine at the corner of the house would also be reduced, and the house owner would be trained to be an animal accustomed to being smoked by fire.

When there were major events such as weddings and funerals in the village, the sheepskin drum would be put to even greater use. At that time, there would be long processions passing through the streets, with priests chanting scriptures, and women wearing brightly colored headscarves to cover their faces. In the evening, the families holding weddings and funerals would offer chickens and sheep with thin wine to entertain guests, and relatives and friends would serve the hosts. The priests would chant scriptures until midnight.

Around the time of the "Fasting Festival," the village would be bustling with the slaughter of cattle and sheep. The villagers would also be busy knocking down coconuts and betel nuts to exchange them for festival items at the market. As a result, the fires in the villages would be extinguished during the day, and huge flames would be lit in front of each "Attap" house at night. Joy flooded the entire countryside, and the peaceful village atmosphere would be broken.

When the waves of "recession" deeply invaded the countryside from the city, the tranquility of the countryside began to fluctuate. Taxes could not be forced out, and soldiers marched into the countryside with guns. While the higher-class Malays remained leisurely, the lower-class commoners were subjected to trampling. The peaceful Malay villages since the time of their ancestors were now threatened, and the color of the world was changing in history!

Today's Malay villages are stirring up ripples, like stones thrown into a calm lake. When the old people and priests can no longer quietly kneel towards the West in the evening, paying homage to their Holy Lord Muhammad's sacred land, I fear that the scenery of the Malay villages will undergo drastic changes again!

Female Leader 170

— Xiang Yu

Under the torches burning with pine resin, a person suddenly fell down, and a scream of pain, mixed with bright red hot blood, burst out together.

"Good technique!"

The people standing in the house watching cried out like wolves, praising.

Another person put away the blood-stained knife, looked arrogantly at the dead person, and then walked to the female leader, whispering:

"Now I have won!"

He raised his head wrapped in black cloth, and raised his proud eyes, as if to say: Please fulfill your promise.

The female leader opened her beautiful big eyes, resolutely drew the two fingers extended in front of her chest outwards, and said quietly:

"I still can't love you."

"Why?"

The victorious man shouted, his face immediately changing to a look of pain. At the same time, the blood-dripping knife suddenly fell to the ground covered with chicken bones and deer bones.

"Because you are injured," the female leader took the remaining half bowl of wine on the table and drank it in one gulp, continuing, with intense enthusiasm, "I want – I want – Heaven, I want to love the bravest man, he will never be injured!"

The dejected man immediately saw his bleeding left wrist, which had been secretly cut by the opponent at the moment the other party fell down. He had endured it and only now felt the pain, and said miserably:

"But I was injured for you."

"But you didn't do it to protect me!"

The female leader turned around, faced the window hung with ivy, and took a deep breath towards the valley shrouded in the dark night. The pine forests spreading over the mountains rose with a great sound of waves, coming closer from afar, roaring.

The man in pain, his face pale, begged in a trembling voice:

"Then, please just use your hand to wrap the wound with cloth!"

The female leader did not speak, but only used two fingers to tidy the hair that had been ruffled by the mountain wind, her eyes still looking at the dark night sleeping outside the window.

"You won't even give me this little bit of pity?"

The female leader still stood with her back to him, coldly saying:

"A person without pity is not worthy of receiving pity."

"Don't I have pity?"

"You have pity?" The female leader suddenly turned around, pointed at the corpse soaked in blood, and said as if cutting through iron, "How did he die? Isn't he still your brother?"

"I am a fool, a fool!"

The begging man wiped his neck with the knife, and fell down dejectedly, bursting out a sorrowful cry.

The female leader raised her sword-like eyebrows, flashing a terrifying light in her eyes, but at the same time, she said charmingly to the crowd:

"No one can possess me alone! I want to be the lover of all of you, because all of you together are the bravest in the world!"

The brothers, stunned by this incident, then hurriedly agreed:

"The leader's words are right!"

At the same time, such a meaning floated in everyone's heart.

"You are really drunk!"

However, in any case, everyone was very happy. Immediately, they followed her onto their horses and went out.

In the dark mountains, the songs of the bandits immediately rose up, but they were soon swallowed by the sound of the pine waves. Thus, the mountain inn covered with bark roofs seemed to have been abandoned, crouching lonely at the bottom of the cliff.

Literary Talks Outside the Door 171

— Hua Yu

(3) How did characters come about?

According to the "Book of Changes," it is clear that knotting ropes came before writing. When our countrymen in the countryside have an important thing to do tomorrow and are afraid of forgetting, they often say, "Tie a knot on your waistband!" So, did our ancient sages also use a long rope, tying a knot for every event? I'm afraid that wouldn't work. They might remember a few knots, but too many would be a mess. Or perhaps that was just like the "Eight Trigrams" of Emperor Fuxi, three ropes in a group. "Qian" is where none of them are knotted, and "Kun" is where each of them has a knot in the middle? I'm afraid that's not right either. Eight groups would be okay, but sixty-four groups would be difficult to remember, let alone five hundred and twelve groups. Only the "knotting words" (Quippug) that remain in Peru, using a horizontal rope with many vertical ropes hanging from it, tied up and down, looking less like a net, but seemingly able to express more meanings. I'm afraid our ancient knotting ropes were like this. But since it has been replaced by writing, and it is not the ancestor of writing, we may as well leave it alone for the time being.

The "Kou Lou Stele" of Xia Yu was forged by Taoists. The oldest writing we can now see in real objects is only the inscriptions on bones and bronze ware from the Shang Dynasty. But these are already very advanced, and it is almost impossible to find an original form. Only on bronzes can we sometimes see a bit of realistic drawings, such as deer and elephants, and from these drawings, we can find clues related to writing: The foundation of Chinese characters is "pictographic."

The wild bull painted in the Altamira cave in Spain is a famous relic of primitive people. Many art historians say that this is precisely "art for art's sake," something that primitive people painted for fun. But this explanation is a bit too "modern," because primitive people did not have as much leisure as the artists of the nineteenth century. His painting of a bull had a reason, which was related to the bull, or to hunting bulls, or to cursing bulls. Even now, people often stare with their mouths open at the cigarette and movie advertisements on the walls of Shanghai. In a primitive society where strange things were rare, one can imagine the sensation that such a miracle would have caused. As they watched, they learned that the thing that was a wild bull could be transferred to another surface using lines, and at the same time they seemed to recognize the character "bull". They also admired the author's talent, but no one asked him to write an autobiography to make money, so the surname was lost. But in society, there was more than one Cangjie. Some carved a picture on a knife handle, some painted some pictures on the doors. Hearts resonated with each other, and words were passed down orally, so that there were more and more words. Once the historians collected them, they could perfunctorily record events. I am afraid that the origin of Chinese characters cannot escape this example.

Naturally, there should be continuous additions later. This is something that historians themselves can do. New characters are inserted among familiar characters, and they are also pictographic, so others can easily guess the meaning of the character. Even now, Chinese is still creating new characters. However, trying to be a new Cangjie will fail. Zhu Yu of Wu and Wu Zetian of Tang all created strange characters, and all their efforts were in vain. Now, the most adept at creating characters are Chinese chemists. The names of many elements and compounds are not easy to recognize, and even the sounds are difficult to pronounce. To be honest, I get a headache as soon as I see them, and I feel that it is far better to use the universally used Latin names. If you don't recognize twenty or so letters, please forgive me for saying it straight: then, you probably won't learn chemistry well either.

The Writer and His Wife 172

— Recorded from the British Bookman

Younger Brother 173

— Zhou Wen

Oh, younger brother, he has been gone from this wicked world for more than a year! Was his death ultimately his happiness or his misfortune? That's "hard to say"; but for me—as long as I have some leisure in my busy schedule, or when I lie in bed with my eyes open late at night, that innocent face of his comes into my mind, as if I heard a "brother" in my ear, and in an instant, that bloody and blurred corpse seems to be placed before my eyes. Oh, I am in pain, I am indignant, I grab my disheveled hair, I clench my thin fists—oh, he is dead!

When my younger brother was a child, he was very naughty. He never seemed to feel that he should study. When Dad died, he was only three years old, and he certainly didn't know that the family was in difficulty. After that, every time the New Year was over, he would hear Mom planning everything for me, and he would just open his innocent big eyes, as if listening to irrelevant stories from overseas—in fact, he was already almost ten years old at that time, and it was time for him to study.

Mom was very capable: although she spat blood, she still had to bite the bullet and resist the bullying from those uncles; he inherited a small shop left by Dad, and stood upright in front of a group of relatives and friends to prop up the scene;...all of this was for us! Her philosophy was: Please, sons, bring her honor in the future! She lived like this. Every year, at the beginning of the year, she would have to go to various places to arrange tuition fees for us; no, it should be said that it was for me alone. Borrowing money was so difficult! Every time she walked out of someone's counter under contemptuous eyes, she could only think: Let's get the older one "on the right track" first. However, my younger brother was left aside.

My younger brother had a rugged body. His face and hands were sunburned red. Short, but imposing, he always opened his big black eyes when he saw someone. I rarely saw him when I came home from school every afternoon. It wasn't until the evening, when Mom lit a small bean-sized vegetable oil lamp for me and supervised me as I studied at night, that he jumped back with a black eye and a swollen face. Sometimes, there were even scratches on his face. Of course, Mom would twist his ears and drag him to the bench to spank him. Before the board even touched his flesh, he would start yelling "Ouch, ouch"; when he was done, a feeling of resentment and indifference would flash across his black and red face. In this way, Mom finally covered her eyes with her sleeves and cried.

Rotary Cup International Tennis Semi-Finals 174

China and the United States Both Win Again Yesterday

Lin Qiu Defeats De Fu and Peng Nifeiqu

～～Record of the Chinese-English Doubles Match～～ 176

(Numerous Highlights) The four players each displayed their unique characteristics. The tense situation was rarely seen before. Qiu Feihai was as consistent as ever, and Lin Baohua was particularly diligent, using either hard serves or twisting, curved serves to great effect. Beautiful shots often left opponents helpless. However, as the two players were cooperating for the first time this year, their coordination was not yet perfect. De Vere's powerful smashes at the net were the best among the four players. (Struggling to Cope) After the start of the game, with bold and vigorous strokes, the sound of rackets colliding resounded, showing sufficient strength. England took the lead with three to one. De Vere's serve resulted in two double faults, and then two more volleys went into the net. China chased back one game. Lin's serve was actually broken, making the situation even more precarious. The opponents were tall and used high-pressure tactics frequently, making it difficult for Lin and Qiu to cope. They were trailing with a score of two to five. After Qiu won his serve, De Vere hit three shots out of bounds, and China managed to add two games in a row, making it four to five, with a momentum to catch up. In the next game, with Lin Baohua serving, they also took the lead with three to one. They only needed to win one more point to make it five to five. Who knew that things would not go as planned? Qiu lost three consecutive points, and Lin's smash went out of bounds, losing with a score of four to six.

(Winning After Fierce Battle) In the second set, there was an even more intense struggle. Bonnicuf served first and lost the game. Qiu Feihai also lost his serve. De Vere gained a lead of two to one with three powerful serves. China tied it to two to two with four to one. Later, it became three to three, three to four, and China was behind. In Lin Baohua's serve, with a slide, it became four to four. They each added one more game, making it five to five, and six to six. Each time England won first, our country followed. In the twelfth game, Lin and Qiu's left and right strikes in front of the net were cunning and skillful, which was a spectacle. As a result, the spirits were lifted, and the momentum shifted, first seizing Bonnicuf's serve. In the next game, our country won three points first, and lost three points in a row. Relying on Lin's two successful high-pressure shots, they turned defeat into victory with a score of eight to six.

(Soaring Upward) In the third set, De Vere served first. In the first four games, each won by serving, making it two to two. Afterwards, there were many suicides. Lin and Qiu's brilliance became more and more prominent, and they handled the situation with ease, winning four consecutive games and winning with a score of six to two, taking very little time. China took the lead with a score of two to one.

(Final Decisive Battle) In the next set, they fell into a difficult battle again, and there was a long competition in each game. De Vere served first again, and the server always won the game, taking turns until five to five. Bonnicuf's serve suddenly failed, and China took the lead with six to five. Unexpectedly, Qiu Feihai's serve also failed, making it six to six again. It was getting late, but the audience's enthusiasm was undiminished, and they clapped and cheered non-stop. The situation became more and more tense. For the sake of prudence, spectators were not allowed to move around the edge of the field, let alone make noise. The whole place was silent. Shen Siliang also advocated changing to a new ball to determine the final outcome. It was Bonnicuf's turn to serve at this time. It was quite inappropriate to change the ball at this time, because it was unfavorable to China. However, because it was the home team, Lin and Qiu could only agree. They were extra careful, and Lin worked extra hard. The opponent guarded the net tightly. Lin skillfully lobbed the ball, disrupting the opponent's strategy. As expected, they seized the game with four to one. Qiu served, and completed it with four to one again. As a result, they won with a score of nine to seven.

Measures for Northeast Students to Go to School and Transfer 187

Educational Bureau Issues Instructions for Notification

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued instructions, stating that, "According to Instruction No. 3329 of the Ministry of Education, it has been found that the number of Northeast youths seeking education is increasing day by day. The school certificates they hold often cannot be recognized as valid, and their actual level is difficult to assess. In order to avoid this difficulty, the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry has been instructed to formulate measures. Now the Office has submitted the measures for Northeast students to go to school and transfer to the Ministry, which has been reviewed and revised by the Ministry in detail. From now on, Northeast students who hold the admission, study, or transfer certificates issued by the Office will be allowed to register for the examination. In addition to notifying the Office and the Peiping Municipal Social Bureau, the relevant measures are attached for your reference and for the compliance of all levels of schools under your jurisdiction." A copy of the Provisional Measures for Northeast Students to Go to School and Transfer is attached. This order is hereby copied and sent to all secondary schools for compliance.

Resolved by Shandong Provincial Government 188

Restore Shandong University Aid

But Reduce 4,000 Yuan Per Month

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Provincial Government, previously stated that due to the financial difficulties of the province, and because Shandong University students did not undergo military training, the Provincial Government's annual disaster relief aid of 360,000 yuan was suspended from July. The central government, Premier Wang Jingwei of the Executive Yuan, and Minister of Education Wang Shijie, had repeatedly telegraphed to request that the aid be maintained as before. Wang also sent Li Shengwu, Director of the International Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, to Lu, carrying Wang's personal letter to Han, reiterating the previous situation. Han, because of the difficulty in rejecting the requests from all parties, and because most of the students of the university were from Qilu, agreed to restore the aid. However, the number hoped for by all circles should be reduced to save public funds. It is proposed to reduce 4,000 yuan per month, which is 312,000 yuan for the whole year. This intention was telegraphed to Wang, and Wang replied, stating that he was very pleased to have maintained the aid to Shandong University, and that the reduction hoped for by all circles would be seriously considered. The university is now expanding the College of Engineering and opening a College of Agriculture, both of which require funds. As the finances of Shandong Province are very difficult, the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance should instruct the university to tighten up its budget. It is hoped that the funds will be allocated as before this year. Han stated that Premier Wang had agreed to reduce the aid to Shandong University by 4,000 yuan per month and should be obeyed. Today (24th), the provincial government's political affairs meeting was held to discuss and approve it.

Dr. Eddy Will Arrive in Shanghai 191

The North China Daily News said that Dr. Eddy, a writer, speaker, and social worker, has recently been invited by the National Committee of the YMCA to come to China and plans to give lectures in 16 places across the country for a period of four months. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai on September 4th on the postal ship Conte Rosso. This is Dr. Eddy's ninth visit to China. Dr. Eddy usually cares about international affairs and has prepared funds to serve as the secretary of the YMCA in India for 15 years, and then as the secretary of the YMCA in Asia for 9 years, working in student groups and political, economic, and social life centers in the Near East and Far East. In 1915, he served as the secretary of the British Army YMCA, and then as the secretary of the American Army YMCA at the front line. After the end of the European War, he helped raise huge sums of money to relieve the Germans in the Ruhr area. Dr. Eddy plans to stay in Shanghai, the capital, Nanchang, and Peiping for two weeks, visiting important figures in education, politics, and religion to learn about Chinese thoughts and all development trends. Therefore, he will start giving lectures in Tianjin on September 18th. The places for lectures in the next four months have been scheduled as follows: North China Tianjin Peiping Baoding Taiyuan, Longhai Border Kaifeng Zhengzhou, West China Chongqing Chengdu, Central China Changsha Nanchang, East China Shanghai Hangzhou Ningbo, South China Xiamen Hong Kong Guangzhou, all 16 places.

Industrial and Commercial Management Tutorial School

Although Shanghai is a thriving center of industry and commerce, there is still a perceived lack of talent in industrial and commercial management.
